Three Proofs That Spatial Location is Existent
Imam Razi gives three proofs that al-hayyiz wa al-jiha is a real existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's three arguments establishing that spatial location is an existent reality, and how this relates to divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Spatial location is real because it has real distinctions that nothingness cannot have.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi begins by proving that spatial location (al-hayyiz) is something existent. This is a crucial step for later arguments about God's transcendence: if location is a real thing, then God cannot be located in it. In this passage, Razi presents three tightly reasoned proofs, each showing that location cannot be pure non-existence. Let's work through them one by one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation. Let the three proofs unfold naturally.
Notice the formal proof structure: 'the proof is from several aspects...'
2
Examine the first proof (difference in quiddity)
Razi argues that different locations (above vs. below) are different in essence. This difference cannot exist in pure nothingness, so location must be real.
He uses the theological fact that God is uniquely associated with 'above' as evidence that directions have real differences.
3
Examine the second proof (sensory pointing)
Directions can be distinguished by pointing (up vs. down). Pure non-existence cannot be pointed to, so directions are real.
This is a common sense argument appealing to direct experience.
4
Examine the third proof (motion of a substance)
When a substance moves from one location to another, the location left and the location entered are different. This difference implies both are real.
This argument relies on the reality of change and distinctness.
5
Draw the conclusion
Razi concludes that spatial location is indeed something existent. Understand how this sets up the later argument that God is not spatially located.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن الحيز والجهة أمر موجود . والدليل عليه من وجوه : الأول : هو أن الأحياز الفوقانية مخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية ، للأحياة التحتانية ، بدليل : أنهم قالوا يجب أن يكون الله تعالى مختصاً بجهة فوق ، ويمتنع حصوله فى سائر الجهات والأحياز – أعنى التحت واليمين واليسار - لولا كونها مختلفة في الحقائق والماهيات ، لامتنع القول بأنه يجب حصوله تعالى في جهة فوق ، ويمتنع حصوله في سائر الجهات. وإذا ثبت أن هذه الأحياز مختلفة في الماهية ، وجب كونها أمورا موجودة . لأن العدم المحض ، يمتنع كونه كذلك . الثاني : هو أن الجهات مختلفة بحسب الإشارات . فإن جهة الفوق متميزة عن جهة التحت في الإشارة . والعدم المحض والنفي الصرف، يمتنع تمييز بعضه عن بعض في الإشارة الحسية . الثالث : إن الجوهر إذا انتقل من حيز إلى حيز ، فالمتروك مغاير لا محالة للمطلوب ، والمنتقل عنه مغاير للمنتقل إليه . فثبت بهذه الوجوه الثلاثة : أن الحيز والجهة أمر موجود .
That spatial location (al-hayyiz wa al-jiha) is something existent. The proof for it is from several aspects: The first: that the upper spatial locations are different in reality and quiddity from the lower spatial locations. Evidence: they said that it is necessary that God be specifically associated with the 'above' direction, and it is impossible for Him to occur in the other directions and spatial locations – meaning the below, the right, and the left – were it not for them being different in realities and quiddities, it would be impossible to say that He must occur in the 'above' direction and cannot occur in the other directions. And when it is established that these spatial locations are different in quiddity, they must be existent things, because pure non-existence cannot be such. The second: that directions are different according to pointing. For the 'above' direction is distinguished from the 'below' direction in pointing. And pure non-existence and absolute negation cannot be distinguished from each other in sensory pointing. The third: that if an atom (jawhar) moves from one spatial location to another, then the abandoned is necessarily different from the sought, and that which is moved from is different from that which is moved to. So it is established by these three aspects that spatial location is something existent.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a proof that spatial location (al-hayyiz wa al-jiha) is an existent thing, not a mere nothing. The author, Imam Razi, presents three arguments. The first argument: different locations (like above and below) are different in quiddity. This is evidenced by the fact that theologians affirm that God must be associated with 'above' and cannot be associated with other directions. If directions were not really different, this affirmation would be meaningless. Since they are different in quiddity, they must be existent, because pure nothingness cannot have distinctions. The second argument: directions are distinguishable by sensory pointing (e.g., pointing up vs. pointing down). Pure non-existence cannot be pointed to or distinguished in this way, so directions must be existent. The third argument: when a substance moves from one place to another, the place left behind is different from the place entered. This difference implies that both places are real things, not nothing. The conclusion: spatial location is something existent.

الجهة
العدم المحض
الإشارة الحسية
الجوهر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These proofs only apply to physical space and have no theological implications.
Correction: Razi uses these proofs to establish that spatial location is a real attribute of created things, which then supports the argument that God transcends location entirely.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the three proofs in this passage?
A) God exists in a spatial location
B) Spatial location is something existent
C) Spatial location is pure non-existence
D) Directions are illusions

Key Takeaway
Spatial location is a real existent thing, as proven by its real distinctions, sensory pointing, and involvement in motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proofs show that space is real because it has distinctions. Yet you affirm that Allah is ‘above’ while also being beyond space. When you raise your hands in du‘a’ and say ‘Allahu akbar’, do you truly feel the transcendence of a Creator who is not confined to any direction, or do you unconsciously imagine Him as far away in a physical sky? What would it mean to pray with the certainty that He is as close as your jugular vein without spatial proximity?
?
The second proof argues that directions are real because they can be pointed to. Think about the direction you face in salah: the qibla is a direction on earth, but Allah is not contained in that direction. How does this truth affect the way you orient your heart when you pray? Is your prayer merely a physical act, or does your soul recognize that the One you worship transcends the very direction you face?
?
The third proof uses motion from one location to another to show that places are real. Your life is a constant movement through places—homes, mosques, graves. If these places are real existents, what does it mean that you will leave them all behind? Are you attached to the 'here' more than to the One who is not bound by any 'here'? How can you live so that your heart's orientation remains fixed on the translocate Lord, even as your body moves through changing spaces?

God Cannot Be in Spatial Location: Three Rational Proofs
Razi enumerates three reasons why God cannot be in spatial location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's existence cannot be limited to spatial location, based on three rational arguments from Imam al-Razi.

Core Idea
If God were in space, He would depend on something contingent — impossible for the Necessary Being.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a rigorous argument demonstrating that God cannot be associated with spatial location. He builds on the foundational principle that what occupies space depends on space, while God is absolutely independent. In this passage, he offers three distinct proofs, each showing that God's association with space leads to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic premise
Recognize that spatial location is independent of what occupies it, but the occupant depends on space. If God were in space, He would be dependent.
This sets up the need for the three proofs.
2
First proof: dependence implies contingency
Anything dependent on another for existence is possible in itself (contingent), but God is necessary in Himself — contradiction.
3
Second proof: spatial location is composite and contingent
Spatial location can be measured and divided, showing it is composed of parts. Composition implies dependence on parts, so it is contingent. If God depended on it, He would be contingent.
4
Third proof: spatial location would be eternal alongside God
If God were eternally in space, space would also be eternal, implying a second eternal being besides God, which is impossible by Islamic consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المسمى بالحيز والجهة ، أمر مستغن في وجوده عما يتمكن ويستقر فيه . وأما الذي يكون مختصاً بالحيز والجهة ، فإنه يكون مفتقرا إلى الحيز والجهة.. فإن الشيء الذي يمكن حصوله في الحيز ، مستحيل عقلا حصوله لا مختصا بالجهة .. فثبت : أنه تعالى لو كان مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، لكان مفتقرا في وجوده إلى الغير . وإنما قلنا : إن ذلك محال لوجوه : الأول : إن المفتقر في وجوده إلى الغير ، يكون بحيث يلزم من عدم ذلك الغير : عدمه . وكل ما كان كذلك ، كان ممكناً لذاته . وذلك في حق واجب الوجود لذاته : محال . الثاني : إن المسمى بالحيز والجهة: أمر متركب من الأجزاء والأبعاض. لما بينا : أنه يمكن تقديره بالذراع والشير، ويمكن وصفه بالزائد والناقص وكل ما كان كذلك ، كان مفتقرا إلى غيره ، والمفتقر إلى غيره : ممكن لذاته . فالشيء المسمى بالحيز والجهة : ممكن لذاته . فلو كان الله تعالى مفتقرا إليه، لكان مفتقرا إلى الممكن ، والمفتقر إلى الممكن أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته . فالواجب إذنه : ممكن لذاته . وهو محال. الثالث : لو كان البارى تعالى أزلا وأبدا مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، لكان الحيز والجهة موجودا في الأزل . فيلزم إثبات قديم غير الله تعالى. وذلك محال بإجماع المسلمين . فثبت بهذه الوجوه : أنه لو كان في الحيز والجهة للزمت هذه المحذورات. فيلزم امتناع كونه تعالى في الحيز والجهة.
Then that which is called spatial location (al-hayyiz wa al-jiha) is independent in its existence from that which occupies and settles in it. But that which is specifically associated with spatial location is dependent upon spatial location. For the thing that can occur in spatial location is rationally impossible to occur not specifically associated with a direction. So it is established: if He—Exalted is He—were specifically associated with spatial location, He would be dependent in His existence upon another. And we say: that is impossible for several reasons: The first: that which is dependent in its existence upon another is such that the non-existence of that other necessitates its own non-existence. And everything that is like that is possible in itself. And that is impossible in the case of the Necessary Existent in itself. The second: that which is called spatial location is a thing composed of parts and segments. Because we have shown that it can be measured by the cubit and the handspan, and can be described as more or less. And everything that is like that is dependent upon another, and that which is dependent upon another is possible in itself. So the thing called spatial location is possible in itself. Thus if God—Exalted is He—were dependent upon it, He would be dependent upon something possible, and that which is dependent upon something possible is more deserving of being possible in itself. So the Necessary would then be possible in itself, which is impossible. The third: if the Creator—Exalted is He—were from eternity to eternity specifically associated with spatial location, then spatial location would exist from eternity. That necessitates affirming an eternal other than God, which is impossible by consensus of the Muslims. So it is established by these reasons that if He were in spatial location, these absurdities would follow. Hence it follows that His—Exalted is He—being in spatial location is impossible.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous one. Having established that spatial location is an existent thing, Razi now argues that God cannot be in space. He reasons that the thing that occupies space is dependent on space, while space itself is independent of what occupies it. Thus if God were in space, He would be dependent on something else. This dependence is impossible for God. Razi gives three specific arguments. First: anything dependent on another for existence is possible in itself, but God is necessary, so dependence is impossible. Second: spatial location is composite (measurable, divisible), so it is contingent. If God depended on it, He would be dependent on a contingent, which would make Him contingent—an impossibility. Third: if God were in space eternally, space would also be eternal, implying another eternal being besides God, which contradicts Islamic consensus. Therefore, God cannot be in spatial location.

واجب الوجود
ممكن لذاته

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'being in space' is a necessary condition for existence, or that God must occupy space to exist.
Correction: Razi shows that occupying space entails dependence and contingency, which cannot apply to God, who is absolutely necessary and independent.

Checkpoint

B) Because it is composite and measurable
C) Because if God were in it eternally, space would be eternal alongside God

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates through three rational proofs that God cannot be associated with spatial location, as it would entail dependence, contingency, or an eternal other-than-God.

Objection to Divine Spatial Location
An objection against Razi's argument on direction and dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main objection that being separate from the world does not entail dependence on a direction.

Core Idea
Separateness from the world is not the same as being physically located.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents an objection from an opponent who argues that describing God as being in a direction is merely a way of saying He is separate from the world—not that He occupies space. The objector claims this does not imply dependence on anything else. We will examine this objection and see how Razi begins his response, though the answer is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: 'If it is said...' (فإن قيل) introduces the opponent's argument.
The passage ends abruptly; Razi's answer is cut off.
2
Identify key terms
Focus on the terms مباين (separate), منفرد (alone), ممتاز (distinct). These are used to redefine 'being in a direction'.
The objector uses these terms to argue that separation is a relational concept, not a real attribute.
3
Understand the objection's logic
The objector says that if God is separate from the world, that is just God's essence—it does not add anything. Therefore, claiming that 'direction' implies dependence is false.
The objection also cites the world's association with space as an analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا معنى لكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، إلا كونه تعالى مباينا عن العالم ، منفردا عنه، ممتازا عنه . وكونه تعالى كذلك ، لا يقتضى أمرا آخر سوى ذات الله تعالى . فبطل قولكم : « لو كان تعالى في الجهة لكان مفتقرا إلى الغير » والذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أن العالم لا نزاع في أنه مختص بالحيز والجهة ، وكونه مختصا بالحيز والجهة لا معنى له إلا
If it is said: There is no meaning to His—Exalted is He—being specifically associated with spatial location except that He—Exalted is He—is separate (mubāyin) from the world, alone (munfarid) from it, distinct (mumtāz) from it. And His being like that does not entail any other thing beyond the essence of God—Exalted is He. Thus your statement falls: 'If He—Exalted is He—were in a direction, He would be dependent upon another.' And what indicates the correctness of what we have mentioned is that the world—there is no dispute that it is specifically associated with spatial location, and its being specifically associated with spatial location has no meaning except...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an objection (فإن قيل) to Razi's previous arguments. The objector argues that 'being in space' or 'in a direction' for God is merely a way of saying that God is separate from the world—not that He is physically located. This separation is not a real attribute; it is just a relational concept. Therefore, it does not imply that God depends on something else. The objector cites that the world itself is associated with space, but that does not mean the world depends on space in a problematic way—so the same could apply to God. The answer is cut off, but presumably Razi would reply that the world's association with space is different because the world is contingent and spatial, while God is not. The page ends mid-sentence, so the argument is incomplete.

Correction: The objector argues that separateness is merely a relational negation—it does not imply spatial location or dependence.

First Proof: Dependence Implies Contingency
Imam Razi presents the first proof that location is impossible for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof that Allah cannot depend on anything, because dependence implies contingency, which contradicts necessary existence.

Core Idea
Dependence on another makes a thing contingent, and what is contingent cannot be God.

Imam Razi begins his proofs for divine transcendence by establishing a basic logical principle: anything that depends on something else for its existence is contingent—it could possibly not exist. Since Allah is the Necessary Existent, He cannot have any such dependence. This short but powerful argument rules out the possibility that Allah occupies a location.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the basic claim.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice that the proof has two conditional statements and a final conclusion. Break it into premises and conclusion.
3
Understand the key terms
Pay attention to 'mumkin li-dhatihi' (contingent in itself) and 'wajib al-wujud li-dhatihi' (necessary of existence in Himself). They are opposites.
4
Apply to location
If Allah were in a location, He would depend on that location. But dependence implies contingency, which is impossible for Allah. Therefore, location is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : إن المفتقر في وجوده إلى الغير ، يكون بحيث يلزم من عدم ذلك الغير : عدمه . وكل ما كان كذلك ، كان ممكناً لذاته . وذلك في حق واجب الوجود لذاته : محال .
The first [proof]: That which depends in its existence upon another is such that from the non-existence of that other, its own non-existence follows. And everything that is like that is contingent in itself (mumkin li-dhatihi). And this, with respect to the Necessary of Existence in Himself (wajib al-wujud li-dhatihi), is impossible.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is the first of three proofs establishing that it is impossible for Allah to be in a location (ḥayyiz or jiha). The argument is: (1) Anything that depends on something else for its existence would cease to exist if that other thing ceased to exist. (2) Anything with such dependence is contingent (mumkin) in itself—it could possibly not exist. (3) But Allah is the Necessary of Existence in Himself (wājib al-wujūd li-dhātihī), meaning His existence is intrinsic and cannot depend on anything else. Therefore, it is impossible for Allah to depend on a location. The logical structure is a simple syllogism: dependence implies contingency, necessity excludes contingency, so location (which would involve dependence) is impossible for the Necessary Being.

Key Terms
مفتقر
الغير
ممكن لذاته
واجب الوجود لذاته
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dependence on a location is a minor attribute that does not affect divinity.
Correction: This proof shows that any dependence necessarily entails contingency, which directly contradicts the necessary and independent nature of Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what follows from something depending on another for its existence?
A) It is eternal.
B) It is contingent in itself.
C) It is necessary in itself.
D) It is a body.

Key Takeaway
Allah's necessary existence excludes any form of dependence, including dependence on a location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You depend on countless things every moment—air, food, people. How does this dependence reveal your own contingency, and what does it mean for your trust in the One who depends on nothing? Will you let that reality shift your reliance entirely onto Him?
?
If you truly believe that Allah’s existence requires no support, no location, no assistance, would you still pray as if He needs your worship? What would change in your salah if you remembered that your worship is for your own need, not His?
?
Consider an area of your life where you feel anxious or insecure. Is it because you are depending on something contingent? How does this proof call you to place your dependence solely on the Necessary Being?

Second Proof: Location is Composite and Contingent
Imam Razi argues that location is composite and contingent, so Allah cannot depend on it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that location is composite and contingent, and why Allah cannot be dependent on location.

Core Idea
Location is composite and contingent; the Necessary Being cannot depend on the contingent.

Imam Razi presents a second argument against Allah being in a location. He shows that location itself is composed of parts and can be measured, making it contingent. If the Necessary Being depended on location, He would depend on a contingent thing—an impossibility. This lesson walks through each step of Razi's proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'if...then'.
2
Identify the premises
List the key premises: location is composite and measurable, composed things are dependent, dependent things are contingent.
3
Trace the dependency chain
Follow the chain: composite → dependent → contingent → Allah cannot depend on contingent because that would make Him contingent.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that Allah cannot be in a location because location is contingent and Allah is necessary.
This reinforces divine transcendence beyond spatial attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن المسمى بالحيز والجهة: أمر متركب من الأجزاء و الأبعاض. لما بينا : أنه يمكن تقديره بالذراع والشير، ويمكن وصفه بالزائد و الناقص وكل ما كان كذلك ، كان مفتقرا إلى غيره ، والمفتقر إلى غيره : ممكن لذاته . فالشيء المسمى بالحيز والجهة : ممكن لذاته . فلو كان الله تعالى مفتقرا إليه، لكان مفتقرا إلى الممكن ، والمفتقر إلى الممكن أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته . فالواجب اذانه : ممكن لذاته . وهو محال.
The second [proof]: That which is called location (al-ḥayyiz) and direction (al-jiha) is a thing composed of parts and members. For it has been shown that it can be measured by the cubit and the handspan, and can be described as greater or lesser. And everything that is like that is dependent upon another, and that which depends upon another is contingent in itself. So the thing called location and direction is contingent in itself. If, therefore, Allah the Exalted were dependent upon it, He would be dependent upon the contingent, and that which depends upon the contingent is more fitting to be contingent in itself. Thus the Necessary [Being] in itself would be contingent in itself—and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof that Allah cannot be in a location. The argument proceeds step by step: (1) Location (ḥayyiz) and direction (jiha) are composite—they can be divided into parts, measured by units like cubits, and described as more or less. (2) Anything composite or measurable is dependent on other things (e.g., its parts and a referent for measure). (3) Dependency indicates contingency (mumkin li-dhātihi). Therefore, location itself is contingent. (4) If Allah (the Necessary Being) were to depend on a location, He would depend on something contingent. (5) Depending on the contingent makes one even more deserving of being contingent. (6) This would lead to the absurd conclusion that the Necessary Being is contingent—impossible. The proof establishes that location is inherently contingent, and since Allah is necessarily existent, He cannot be in any spatial context.

Key Terms
الحيز
الجهة
مركب
تقدير بالذراع
مفتقر
ممكن لذاته
واجب لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that location is a simple notion without parts.
Correction: Razi shows location is composite because it can be measured and described as greater or lesser, indicating it has parts.

Checkpoint
What is the key characteristic of location (al-ḥayyiz) that proves it is contingent?
A) It is eternal.
B) It is composite and measurable.
C) It is a mental concept.
D) It is identical to Allah.

Key Takeaway
Location is contingent because it is composite and dependent; therefore, the Necessary Being cannot depend on location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you subconsciously assign Him a place in your mind? How does this proof challenge that tendency, and what concrete steps will you take to purge such spatial thinking from your concept of Allah?
?
The proof shows that depending on anything contingent makes one contingent. What dependencies in your own life—on people, possessions, or status—are you clinging to that you know are contingent? How can you shift your reliance solely to the Necessary Being starting today?
?
Imam Razi argues that location is composite and dependent. Consider your own attachment to a physical mosque or prayer space. If you feel spiritually lost when not in that place, what does that reveal about your understanding of Allah's transcendence? How will you worship Him without spatial dependence beginning with your next prayer?

Third Proof: Location Would Imply Another Eternal Being
Imam Razi's third proof using the impossibility of a co-eternal location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof that Allah cannot be in a location because it would imply an eternal co-existing entity, which contradicts Islamic consensus.

Core Idea
If Allah were spatial, the space would also be eternal, making two gods.

Imam Razi presents his third and final proof that Allah is not subject to space or direction. This argument appeals directly to the consensus of Muslims that nothing else is eternal besides Allah. Read carefully how Razi builds this concise but powerful proof from the impossibility of a co-eternal location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English to get the flow of the argument. Notice the key terms: azal, qadim, ijmāʿ.
2
Identify the logical steps
Break down the argument: premise 1: if Allah is in location from eternity, then location is eternal; premise 2: that means another eternal being besides Allah; premise 3: this is impossible by consensus. Conclusion: Allah cannot be in location.
3
Reflect on the use of consensus
Consider why Razi uses ijmāʿ as a decisive authority. How does this argument differ from the previous two?
Consensus is a strong source of certainty in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كان البارى تعالى أزلا وأبدا مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، لكان الحيز والجهة موجودا في الأزل . فيلزم إثبات قديم غير الله تعالى. وذلك محال بإجماع المسلمين . فثبت بهذه الوجوه : أنه لو كان في الحيز والجهة للزمت هذه المحذورات. فيلزم امتناع كونه تعالى في الحيز والجهة .
The third [proof]: If the Creator (al-Bāriʾ) the Exalted were, from pre-eternity (azalan) and forever (abadan), particularized by location (al-ḥayyiz) and direction (al-jiha), then location and direction would exist in pre-eternity (al-azal). This necessitates affirming an eternal being (qadīm) other than Allah the Exalted. And that is impossible by the consensus of the Muslims (ijmāʿ al-Muslimīn). Therefore, it is established by these proofs that if He were in location and direction, these impossibilities would follow. Hence it follows that it is impossible for Him the Exalted to be in location and direction.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof against Allah being in a location, which is based on the consensus of Muslims regarding Tawḥīd. The argument: (1) If Allah were in a location from eternity (both beginningless and endless), that location would also have to exist from eternity. (2) This would mean affirming another eternal being (qadīm) besides Allah. (3) But the entire Muslim community agrees that affirming an eternal entity besides Allah is impossible (shirk). (4) Therefore, it is impossible for Allah to be spatial or directional. The proof appeals to Islamic consensus (ijmāʿ) as a decisive authority. The three proofs together establish the transcendence of Allah beyond space and direction.

مختصا بالحيز والجهة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah is in a location, that location must be created and thus not eternal, avoiding the problem.
Correction: The argument is that if Allah is always in a location from eternity, then that location exists from eternity, making it uncreated and co-eternal with Allah, which contradicts tawhid.

Checkpoint

A) The location would be created.
B) The location would be eternal like Allah.
C) Allah would change.
D) The world would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The third proof uses consensus to argue that a spatial Allah would require an eternal location, which is tantamount to shirk.

The proof relies on the consensus of Muslims (ijmaʿ). Is there any attribute of Allah about which you hold a personal interpretation that contradicts the consensus of the righteous predecessors? Are you willing to abandon that interpretation for the sake of sound belief?
?
If Allah is not in any direction, then He is closer to you than your jugular vein without being 'in' you. Does your daily worship reflect this reality? What practical steps can you take to increase your awareness of Allah's all-encompassing presence?

Refuting the Objection: Location as Abstract Separation
Imam Razi refutes an objection about divine location by clarifying the meaning of separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi distinguishes between two meanings of 'separation' (essential vs. spatial) to defend God's transcendence and refute the objection that location is merely an abstract distinction.

Core Idea
Separation from the world does not require a spatial location—unless that's what you mean by it.

In this passage, Razi confronts an objection that tries to reduce divine location to a mere abstract distinction. The objection claims that saying Allah is 'separate' from the world does not imply any real location. Razi's answer is layered: first, he reaffirms that location is real; second, he unpacks the ambiguity of 'separation' to show that if spatial separation is meant, it does entail a real location—something impossible for Allah. This distinction is crucial for preserving divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objector's argument: that being 'separate' from the world is just an abstract relation, not a real location. Notice how the objector uses the world as an analogy.
The objector's point seems plausible—why should separation imply a real entity?
2
Identify Razi's two-part answer
Razi's answer has two main parts: first, he asserts that location and direction are real things proven by decisive arguments. Second, he addresses the claim about 'separation' by clarifying its possible meanings.
This two-pronged approach is typical in kalam dialectics.
3
Understand the ambiguity of 'separation'
Razi explains that words like 'separate' (mubāyin), 'isolated' (munfarid), and 'distinguished' (mumtāz) can mean either difference in essence (which is fine) or spatial distinction (which implies a real location). The opponent intends the latter, but that requires a real location and dependence.
This is the key logical move: the objection confuses two meanings.
4
See the proof and conclusion
Razi concludes that if the opponent means spatial distinction, then location must be real, and Allah's need for it is impossible. He also notes that bodies' need for location is not problematic because they are contingent.
The difference (farq) between Allah and bodies is that need for location is impossible for the Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا معنى لكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، إلا كونه تعالى مباينا عن العالم ، منفردا عنه، ممتازا عنه . وكونه تعالى كذلك ، لا يقتضى أمرا آخر سوى ذات الله تعالى . فبطل قولكم : « لو كان تعالى في الجهة لكان مفتقرا إلى الغير ، والذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أن العالم لا نزاع في أنه مختص بالحيز والجهة ، وكونه مختصا بالحيز والجهة لا معنى له إلا كون البعض منفردا عن البعض وتمتازا عنه . وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا فلا يجوز مثله في كون البارى تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز ؟ والجواب : أما قوله : « الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجودا ، فجوابه : إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة أنها أشياء موجودة وبعد قيام البراهين على صحته، لا يبقى في صحته شك . وأما قوله : ( المراد من كونه مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم ، أو ممتازا عنه أو مباينا عنه ، قلنا : هذه الألفاظ كلها مجملة ، فإن الانفراد والامتيار والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك ما لا نزاع فيه . ولكنه لا يقتضى الجهة . والدليل على ذلك : هو أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفا لحقيقة الحيز والجهة وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة . فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى من الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى، وإلا لزم التسلسل . وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة ، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه بأنه هنا أو هناك . وهذا هو مراد الخصم من قوله : «إنه (تعالى) مباين عن العالم أو منفرد عنه ، أو ممتاز عنه ، إلا أنا بينا بالبرامين القاطعة أن هذا يقتضى كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا، ويقتضى أن المتحيز محتاج إلى الحيز . وقوله : « الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز، فنقول : غاية ما في الياب أن يقال : الأجسام تحتاج إلى شيء آخر . وهذا غير ممتنع . أما كونه تعالى محتاجا في وجوده إلى شيء آخر ، فمتنع . فظهر الفرق وبالله التوفيق
If it is said: "There is no meaning to His being particularized by location and direction except that He is separate (mubāyin) from the world, solitary (munfarid) from it, distinguished (mumtāz) from it. And His being like that does not necessitate any other thing besides His essence. Thus your statement—'If He were in a direction, He would be dependent upon another'—is invalid. And what indicates the correctness of what we have mentioned is that the world, without dispute, is particularized by location and direction, and its particularization by location and direction has no meaning except that some parts are solitary from others and distinguished from it. And if we understand this meaning here, is it not permissible that the same applies to the Creator being particularized by direction and location?" The answer: As for his statement, "Location and direction are not existing things," we reply: We have demonstrated with decisive proofs (barāhīn qāṭiʿa) that they are existing things, and after the establishment of proofs for their reality, no doubt remains. And as for his statement, "What is meant by His being particularized by location and direction is that He is separate from the world, distinguished from it, or isolated from it," we say: All these expressions are ambiguous (mujmala). For isolation, distinction, and separation may be mentioned with the intention of difference in quiddity and essence (al-mukhālafa fī al-ḥaqīqa wa al-māhiyya). That is not disputed. But it does not necessitate direction. The evidence for that is that the essence of Allah is different from the essence of location and direction, and this difference and separation is not by way of direction. For the distinction of the essence of Allah from direction is not by another direction—otherwise an infinite regress would occur. And these expressions may be mentioned with the intention of distinction in direction (al-imtiyāz fī al-jiha): that is, a thing being such that it can be pointed to as 'here' or 'there'. And this is what the opponent means by his statement, 'He is separate from the world, isolated from it, or distinguished from it.' However, we have demonstrated with decisive proofs that this necessitates that location is an existing thing, and that what is located (al-mutaḥayyiz) is in need of the location. And his statement, 'Bodies are located in locations,' we say: The most that can be said is that bodies need something else. That is not impossible. But that He is in need of something else for His existence is impossible. Thus the difference is clear. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its detailed answer, forming a dialectical exchange. The objector argues that „being in a location“ is just a metaphor for God‘s separation from the world—it does not imply a real entity. He uses the world as an example: bodies are spatially distinguished, but that only means parts are distinct, not a separate substance called location. Therefore, saying Allah is separate from the world does not entail a real location. Razi‘s answer unfolds in two parts. First, he reaffirms that location and direction are real, existing things, proven by decisive arguments (barāhīn qāṭiʿa). Second, he distinguishes two meanings of words like „separation“ (mubāyana), „isolation“ (infirād), and „distinction“ (imtiyāz): (a) difference in essence/quiddity—that Allah‘s essence is unlike the world, which all Muslims affirm but does not imply direction; and (b) spatial distinction, i.e., being able to point to something as „here“ or „there“. The opponent intends the second meaning, but that meaning necessarily involves a real direction/location, which (as shown earlier) is an existent thing. Furthermore, if Allah were spatially distinct, He would need that location—a need impossible for the Necessary Being. Razi adds that bodies‘ need for locations is not problematic because they are contingent, but Allah‘s need would be. Thus the difference is clear: bodily location involves need, but divine transcendence precludes any such need. The response preserves the transcendence (tanzīh) of Allah.

Key Terms
مباين
منفرد
ممتاز
مخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية
الامتياز في الجهة
التسلسل
متحيز
براهين قاطعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying Allah is 'separate from the world' is merely a figurative expression that does not imply any real location or dependence.
Correction: Razi shows that if 'separate' is taken to mean spatial distinction, it necessarily implies a real location and dependence, which is impossible for Allah. If it means essential difference, it is acceptable but does not involve direction.

Checkpoint
How does Razi respond to the objection that 'being separate from the world' does not entail a real location?
A) He admits it and changes the topic.
B) He distinguishes between essential difference and spatial distinction, noting that only the latter implies a real location.
C) He says the objection is irrelevant.
D) He claims that all separation is spatial.

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that divine transcendence does not allow spatial location, and ambiguous terms like 'separation' must be carefully defined to avoid attributing need to the Necessary Being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use phrases like 'Allah is above' or 'Allah is with us,' do you ever pause to examine whether your heart attaches a spatial meaning to those words? What might this reveal about your hidden assumptions regarding Allah's nature?
?
Have you ever defended a correct Islamic belief using an argument that was imprecise or ambiguous? How did you feel when you later realized the flaw? This lesson shows the danger of ambiguous language—what commitment will you make to ensure your words about Allah are as precise as your intentions?
?

Razi builds a case on divine self-sufficiency and the contingency of location. Do you truly feel in your soul that Allah needs nothing—not even your worship? How would it change your worship if you fully internalized His absolute independence?

Affirming the Existence of Space and Direction
Razi responds to the objection by affirming existence of space and direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's assertion that space and direction are existent realities, proven by decisive proofs, and why this counters the opponent's premise.

Core Idea
Space and direction are real, established by decisive proofs.

The opponent argues that if one thing can be separate from another, why can't God be specified with direction? Razi's first response is to reject the opponent's premise that space and direction are non-existent. He affirms that they are existent entities, proven by decisive arguments, leaving no room for doubt. This lesson focuses on that initial refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the opponent's analogy and Razi's direct response.
The opponent's objection is the first sentence; Razi's answer follows 'والجواب:'.
2
Identify the opponent's premise
The opponent claims that space and direction are not existent things. Razi counters by asserting they are existent.
3
Reflect on Razi's claim
Razi says decisive proofs have established the existence of space and direction. Consider why this is a foundational move for the discussion.
This sets the stage for the next lesson on terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كون البعض منفردا عن البعض وتمتازا عنه. وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا فلا يجوز مثله في كون الباري تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز؟ والجواب: أما قوله: «الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجودا»، فجوابه: إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة أنها أشياء موجودة، وبعد قيام البراهين على صحته لا يبقى في صحته شك. وأما قوله: (المراد من كونه مختصا بالحيز والجهة، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم، أو ممتازا عنه، أو مباينا عنه)، قلنا: هذه الألفاظ كلها مجملة، فإن الانفراد والامتياز والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك ما لا نزاع فيه. ولكنه لا يقتضي الجهة. والدليل على ذلك: هو أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفة لحقيقة الحيز والجهة، وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة. فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى من الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى، وإلا لزم التسلسل. وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه بأنه هنا أو هناك. وهذا هو مراد الخصم من قوله: «إنه تعالى مباين عن العالم أو منفرد عنه، أو ممتاز عنه»، إلا أنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة أن هذا يقتضي كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا، ويقتضي أن المتحيز محتاج إلى الحيز. وقوله: «الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز»، فنقول: غاية ما في الباب أن يقال: الأجسام تحتاج إلى شيء آخر. وهذا غير ممتنع. أما كونه تعالى محتاجا في وجوده إلى شيء آخر، فممتنع. فظهر الفرق. وبالله التوفيق.
That one thing is separate from another and distinct from it. And if we understand this meaning here, then the like of it is not allowed regarding the fact that the Most High Creator is specified with direction and space? And the answer: As for his statement: 'Space and direction are not an existent thing,' its answer is: We have demonstrated with decisive proofs that they are existent things, and after the proofs have been established for their correctness, no doubt remains about their correctness. And as for his statement: 'What is meant by His being specified with space and direction is that He, Most High, is separate from the world, or distinct from it, or other than it,' we say: These expressions are all ambiguous, for 'separateness,' 'distinction,' and 'otherness' may be mentioned and by them is intended opposition in reality and essence. That is undisputed. But it does not necessitate direction. The proof of that is: The reality of the essence of God Most High is opposed to the reality of space and direction, and this opposition and otherness is not by direction. For the distinction of the essence of God Most High from direction is not by another direction, otherwise infinite regress would follow. And these expressions may be mentioned and by them is intended distinction in direction, which is the thing being such that it is valid to point to it as 'here' or 'there.' And this is what the opponent intends by his statement: 'He, Most High, is other than the world or separate from it, or distinct from it,' except that we have demonstrated with decisive proofs that this necessitates that that space is an existent thing, and it necessitates that that which occupies space is in need of space. And his statement: 'Bodies occur in spaces,' so we say: The utmost in the matter is that it is said: Bodies need something else. And this is not impossible. As for Him, Most High, being in need in His existence of something else, that is impossible. So the difference became clear. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent argues: if we can conceive of one thing being separate and distinct from another (e.g., two bodies), why can't we conceive of God being separate from the world in terms of direction and space? Razi first refutes the premise that space and direction are not existent things—he states that decisive proofs have shown they are existent. Then he addresses the main objection by clarifying the ambiguity of terms like 'separateness' (infirād), 'distinction' (imtiyāz), and 'otherness' (mubāyana). He explains that these terms can mean two different things: (1) difference in reality and essence, which is true of God relative to the world but does not imply direction; (2) spatial distinction, where a thing can be pointed to as 'here' or 'there'. The opponent intends the second meaning, but Razi argues that this would require the space to be an existent entity and the occupant to be in need of that space. The opponent then objects that bodies are in spaces, but Razi distinguishes: bodies needing a space is not impossible, but God needing something else is impossible. Thus the difference between bodies and God is clear.

الجهة (al-jiha)

Two Meanings of 'Separation' from the World
Razi clarifies the ambiguity of terms and distinguishes essential vs. spatial otherness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's distinction between essential otherness and spatial otherness, and why spatial otherness is impossible for God.

Core Idea
'Separateness' can mean difference in essence, not spatial distance.

Having affirmed the existence of space, Razi now addresses the opponent's use of terms like 'separate,' 'distinct,' and 'other.' He explains that these words are ambiguous: they can refer to difference in essence (which is true for God) or spatial separation (which the opponent intends). He then proves that spatial separation would lead to an infinite regress or need for space, and distinguishes God from bodies. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Razi breaks down the opponent's argument.
The passage starts with 'وأما قوله:' and continues to the end.
2
Identify the two meanings of 'mubāyana'
Razi lists two meanings: (1) difference in essence and reality, and (2) spatial distinction (pointable as 'here' or 'there'). Identify each.
3
Understand the proof against spatial otherness
Razi argues that if God were spatially distinct from direction, that distinction would require another direction, leading to an infinite regress. Follow this logic.
Also note the consequence: the occupant needs a space, which is impossible for God.
4
See the distinction from bodies
The opponent brings up bodies existing in spaces. Razi responds that bodies needing space is not impossible, but God needing something is. Compare.
This shows the difference between contingent and necessary being.

كون البعض منفردا عن البعض وتمتازا عنه. وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا فلا يجوز مثله في كون الباري تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز؟ والجواب: أما قوله: «الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجودا»، فجوابه: إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة أنها أشياء موجودة، وبعد قيام البراهين على صحته لا يبقى في صحته شك. وأما قوله: (المراد من كونه مختصا بالحيز والجهة، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم، أو ممتازا عنه، أو مباينا عنه)، قلنا: هذه الألفاظ كلها مجملة، فإن الانفراد والامتياز والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك ما لا نزاع فيه. ولكنه لا يقتضي الجهة. والدليل على ذلك: هو أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفة لحقيقة الحيز والجهة، وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة. فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى من الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى، وإلا لزم التسلسل. وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه بأنه هنا أو هناك. وهذا هو مراد الخصم من قوله: «إنه تعالى مباين عن العالم أو منفرد عنه، أو ممتاز عنه»، إلا أنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة أن هذا يقتضي كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا، ويقتضي أن المتحيز محتاج إلى الحيز. وقوله: «الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز»، فنقول: غاية ما في الباب أن يقال: الأجسام تحتاج إلى شيء آخر. وهذا غير ممتنع. أما كونه تعالى محتاجا في وجوده إلى شيء آخر، فممتنع. فظهر الفرق. وبالله التوفيق.
That one thing is separate from another and distinct from it. And if we understand this meaning here, then the like of it is not allowed regarding the fact that the Most High Creator is specified with direction and space? And the answer: As for his statement: 'Space and direction are not an existent thing,' its answer is: We have demonstrated with decisive proofs that they are existent things, and after the proofs have been established for their correctness, no doubt remains about their correctness. And as for his statement: 'What is meant by His being specified with space and direction is that He, Most High, is separate from the world, or distinct from it, or other than it,' we say: These expressions are all ambiguous, for 'separateness,' 'distinction,' and 'otherness' may be mentioned and by them is intended opposition in reality and essence. That is undisputed. But it does not necessitate direction. The proof of that is: The reality of the essence of God Most High is opposed to the reality of space and direction, and this opposition and otherness is not by direction. For the distinction of the essence of God Most High from direction is not by another direction, otherwise infinite regress would follow. And these expressions may be mentioned and by them is intended distinction in direction, which is the thing being such that it is valid to point to it as 'here' or 'there.' And this is what the opponent intends by his statement: 'He, Most High, is other than the world or separate from it, or distinct from it,' except that we have demonstrated with decisive proofs that this necessitates that that space is an existent thing, and it necessitates that that which occupies space is in need of space. And his statement: 'Bodies occur in spaces,' so we say: The utmost in the matter is that it is said: Bodies need something else. And this is not impossible. As for Him, Most High, being in need in His existence of something else, that is impossible. So the difference became clear. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent argues: if we can conceive of one thing being separate and distinct from another (e.g., two bodies), why can't we conceive of God being separate from the world in terms of direction and space? Razi first refutes the premise that space and direction are not existent things—he states that decisive proofs have shown they are existent. Then he addresses the main objection by clarifying the ambiguity of terms like 'separateness' (infirād), 'distinction' (imtiyāz), and 'otherness' (mubāyana). He explains that these terms can mean two different things: (1) difference in reality and essence, which is true of God relative to the world but does not imply direction; (2) spatial distinction, where a thing can be pointed to as 'here' or 'there'. The opponent intends the second meaning, but Razi argues that this would require the space to be an existent entity and the occupant to be in need of that space. The opponent then objects that bodies are in spaces, but Razi distinguishes: bodies needing a space is not impossible, but God needing something else is impossible. Thus the difference between bodies and God is clear.

المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية (al-mukhālafa fī al-ḥaqīqa wa al-māhiyya)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul)

Misconception: That any kind of 'otherness' (mubāyana) implies spatial separation.
Correction: Razi shows that otherness can mean difference in essence, which does not imply spatial direction.

Third Proof: Impossibility of Infinite Dimension
Razi enumerates three possibilities for a body in direction and refutes the first via geometric contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's third proof that God cannot be in a direction, particularly the geometric argument against infinite extension.

Core Idea
An infinite dimension leads to a logical contradiction, proving its impossibility.

Imam Razi continues his arguments for God's transcendence beyond direction. Here he presents a trilemma: if God were in a direction, He would be either infinite from all sides, infinite from some and finite from others, or finite from all sides. He then refutes the first option using a geometric proof that an infinite dimension is impossible. This lesson examines that proof and its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three divisions
Carefully read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Razi states three possibilities for a being that occupies a direction. Write them down.
The three divisions are: infinite from all sides, infinite from some sides and finite from others, finite from all sides.
2
Understand the geometric proof against the first division
Focus on the argument starting with 'the first: that the existence of a dimension with no end is impossible.' Follow the steps: assume an infinite line and a finite parallel line moving to alignment; this requires a first point of alignment, but the infinite line has no first point.
3
Reflect on the concept of 'first point of alignment'
Why does the infinite line prevent a first point? Because for any point, there is always a point above it, so no point can be the first to be aligned. This is a contradiction.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Since the first possibility is impossible, and the other two are also impossible (though not detailed here), the original claim that God is in a direction is false. This supports tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الثالث في بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز: أنه لو كان تعالى مختصا بحيز وجهة لكان: إما أن يقال: إنه غير متناه من جميع الجوانب، أو يقال: إنه غير متناه من بعض الجوانب، ومتناه من بعض الجوانب، أو يقال إنه متناه من كل الجوانب. والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكونه مختصا بجهة وحيز باطل. أما قولنا: إنه يمتنع أن يكون غير متناه من جميع الجوانب. فيدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إن وجود بعد لا نهاية له محال. والدليل عليه أن فرض بعد غير متناه يفضي إلى المحال، فوجب أن يكون محالا. وإنما قلنا إنه يفضي إلى المحال، لأنا إذا فرضنا بعدا غير متناه، وفرضنا بعدا آخر متناهيا، موازيا له، ثم زال الخط المتناهي الموازي من الموازاة إلى المسامتة. نقول: هذا يقتضي أن يحصل في الخط الأول الذي هو غير متناه نقطة هي أول نقط المسامتة. وذلك الخط المتناهي ما كان مسامتا للخط غير المتناهي، ثم صار مسامتا له. فكانت هذه المسامتة في أول أوان حدوثها، لابد وأن تكون مع نقطة معينة، فتكون تلك النقطة أول نقط المسامتة. لكن كون ذلك الخط غير متناه يمنع من ذلك. لأن المسامتة مع النقطة المسامتة تحصل قبل المسامتة مع النقطة التحتانية. وإذا كان الخط غير متناه، فلا نقطة فيه إلا وفوقها نقطة أخرى. وذلك يمنع من حصول المسامتة في المرة الأولى مع نقطة معينة. فثبت أن هذا يقتضي أن يحصل في الخط غير المتناهي نقطة هي أول نقط المسامتة.
The third proof in explaining that it is impossible that He, Most High, be specified with direction and space: That if He, Most High, were specified with a space and a direction, then: Either it is said: He is infinite from all sides, or it is said: He is infinite from some sides and finite from some sides, or it is said: He is finite from all sides. And the three divisions are invalid, so the statement that He is specified with a direction and space is invalid. As for our statement: It is impossible that He be infinite from all sides. There are proofs for it: The first: That the existence of a dimension with no end is impossible. The proof of it is that the assumption of an infinite dimension leads to an impossibility, so it must be impossible. And we only say it leads to an impossibility, because if we assume an infinite dimension, and we assume another finite dimension parallel to it, then the finite parallel line moves from parallelism to alignment. We say: This necessitates that in the first line which is infinite, there occurs a point that is the first point of alignment. And that finite line was not aligned with the infinite line, then it became aligned with it. So this alignment at its first moment of occurrence must be with a specific point, so that point becomes the first point of alignment. But the fact that that line is infinite prevents that. Because the alignment with the upper point occurs before the alignment with the lower point. And if the line is infinite, there is no point in it except that above it is another point. And that prevents the occurrence of the alignment at the first time with a specific point. So it is established that this necessitates that in the infinite line there occurs a point that is the first point of alignment.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof against God being in a direction. Razi begins by stating that if God were in a space/direction, He must be either (1) infinite from all sides, (2) infinite from some sides and finite from others, or (3) finite from all sides. All three are invalid, so the claim is invalid. He then proceeds to refute the first possibility using a geometric argument. He assumes an infinite dimension (line) and a finite parallel line that moves from being parallel to being aligned (i.e., directly opposite). At the first moment of alignment, there must be a specific point on the infinite line that is the first point of alignment. However, because the line is infinite, for any point there is always another point above it, so there cannot be a 'first' point of alignment. This contradiction shows that an infinite dimension is impossible. The argument is cut off before discussing the other two possibilities, but the overall proof is that the impossibility of the first division suffices to refute the claim, as the other divisions are also impossible.

متناه (mutanāhin)

نقطة (nuqta)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think infinite extension is possible or that God could be in a direction.
Correction: Razi shows that the very concept of an infinite physical dimension is logically contradictory, thus God cannot have any direction.

D) Necessary, impossible, possible

Key Takeaway
Razi's geometric proof demonstrates that the concept of an infinite physical dimension is logically contradictory, supporting the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi used a rigorous geometric proof to show that Allah cannot be contained in any direction. Have you ever imagined Allah as being 'up there' in the sky or in some direction? What would it cost you to let go of that mental image and worship a God who transcends all spatial concepts?
?
If a finite line can never find a first point of alignment with an infinite line, what does that tell you about your own attempts to 'align' your finite understanding with the infinite reality of Allah? In what area of your life have you assumed that your conception of Allah is complete or accurate?
?
The proof shows that an infinite dimension leads to a logical contradiction. How often do you try to 'measure' or 'locate' Allah within the finite frames of your own expectations, emotions, or circumstances? What would it mean to submit to a God who cannot be contained by any direction or limit?

Third Proof: Allah Cannot Be Confined to a Direction (Part 1)
Imam Razi presents a logical division and refutation of spatial attributes for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical division used by Imam Razi to refute spatial attributes for Allah, and the geometric argument demonstrating the impossibility of an infinite extended magnitude.

Core Idea
Assuming Allah has a direction leads to logical contradictions, such as an impossible infinite extension.

Imam Razi employs a rigorous method of exhaustive division and refutation to show that Allah cannot occupy space. He divides the possibilities into three and disproves the first two, starting with a geometric argument that an infinite extended magnitude is impossible. This lesson covers the first two divisions and their refutations, establishing a key foundation for divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three divisions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Imam Razi divides the assumption of Allah being in a direction into three mutually exclusive cases. Write them down.
The three cases are: infinite from all sides, infinite from some sides and finite from others, finite from all sides.
2
Understand the geometric argument against infinite extension
Focus on the first proof (wajh) for the first division. Imagine an infinite line and a finite line becoming aligned. Why does this lead to a contradiction? Trace the reasoning step by step.
The key point: an infinite line has no first point, but alignment requires a first point of contact.
3
Examine the second and third proofs for the first division
The second proof is a meta-argument: if infinite extension were possible, the proof of the world's finiteness would collapse by consensus. The third proof is theological: if Allah were infinite in all directions, nothing would be devoid of Him, leading to absurdities like mixture with impurities.
4
Analyze the refutation of the second division
The second division (infinite from some sides, finite from others) is refuted by two aspects: (1) the same proof against infinite extension applies to any infinite side, and (2) if the infinite and finite sides are equal in essence, then the finite side would also be infinite, a contradiction. Note that the text is truncated, so this argument is incomplete.

ومتناه من بعض الجوانب، أو يقال إنه متناه من كل الجوانب. والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكونه مختصا بجهة وحيز باطل. أما قولنا: إنه يمتنع أن يكون غير متناه من جميع الجوانب. فيدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إن وجود بعد لا نهاية له محال، والدليل عليه أن فرض بعد غير متناه يفضي إلى المحال، فوجب أن يكون محالا. وإنما قلنا إنه يفضي إلى المحال، لأنا إذا فرضنا بعدا غير متناه، وفرضنا بعدا آخر متناهيا، موازيا له، ثم مسامتا له. فكانت هذه المسامتة في أول أوان حدوثها، لابد وأن تكون مع نقطة معينة فتكون تلك النقطة أول نقط المسامتة. لكن كون ذلك الخط غير متناه، يمنع من ذلك. لأن المسامتة مع النقطة العليا، تحصل قبل المسامتة مع النقطة التحتانية. وإذا كان الخط غير متناه، فلا نقطة فيه إلا وفوقها نقطة أخرى. وذلك يمنع من حصول المسامتة في المرة الأولى، مع نقطة معينة. فثبت أن هذا يقتضي أن يحصل في الخط الغير المتناهي نقطة، هي أول نقط المسامتة، وأن لا يحصل. وهذا المحال إنما لزم من فرضنا أن ذلك الخط غير متناه، فوجب أن يكون ذلك محالا. فثبت: أن القول بوجود بعد غير متناه محال. الوجه الثاني: هو أنه إذا كان القول بوجود بعد غير متناه ليس محالا، فعند هذا لا يمكن إقامة الدليل على أن العالم متناه بكليته. وذلك باطل بالإجماع. الوجه الثالث: إنه لو كان تعالى غير متناه من جميع الجوانب، وجب أن لا يخلو شيء من الجهات والأحياز عن ذاته، وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون العالم مخالطا بأجزاء ذاته، وأن تكون القاذورات والنجاسات كذلك، وهذا لا يقوله عاقل. أما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: إنه غير متناه من بعض الجوانب ومتناه من سائر الجوانب. فهو أيضا باطل بوجهين: الأول: إن البرهان الذي ذكرناه على امتناع بعد غير متناه قائم. سواء كان قد قيل: إنه غير متناه من كل الجوانب، أو من بعض الجوانب. الثاني: إن الجانب الذي فرض أنه غير متناه، والجانب الذي فرض متناه. إما أن يكونا متساويين في الحقيقة والماهية، وإما أن لا يكونا كذلك. أما القسم الأول فإنه يقتضي أن يصح على كل واحد من هذين
The third proof in explaining that it is impossible for the Exalted to be specific to a place and direction: that if the Exalted were specific to a place and direction, He would not be free. It is either said: He is infinite from all sides, or said: He is infinite from some sides and finite from some sides, or said: He is finite from all sides. And the three divisions are invalid, so the statement that He is specific to a direction and place is invalid. As for our statement: it is impossible for Him to be infinite from all sides. There are proofs for it: The first: that the existence of an extension with no end is impossible, and the proof for it is that the assumption of an infinite extension leads to impossibility, so it must be impossible. And we said that it leads to impossibility because if we assume an infinite extension, and we assume another finite extension, parallel to it, then the finite parallel line deviates from parallelism to alignment. We say: this necessitates that in the first line, which is infinite, there occurs a point that is the first point of alignment. And that finite line was not aligned with the infinite line, then it became aligned with it. So this alignment in the first moment of its occurrence must be with a specific point, so that point becomes the first point of alignment. But the fact that that line is infinite prevents that. Because alignment with the upper point occurs before alignment with the lower point. And if the line is infinite, there is no point in it except that above it is another point. And that prevents the occurrence of alignment in the first time with a specific point. So it is established that this necessitates that in the infinite line there occurs a point that is the first point of alignment, and that it does not occur. And this impossibility arose only from our assumption that that line is infinite, so that must be impossible. So it is established that the statement that there exists an infinite extension is impossible. The second proof: is that if the statement that there exists an infinite extension were not impossible, then it would not be possible to establish the proof that the world is entirely finite. And that is invalid by consensus. The third proof: that if the Exalted were infinite from all sides, then nothing of directions and places would be devoid of His essence, and then it would follow that the world would be mixed with parts of His essence, and that filth and impurities would be like that, and no rational person would say this. As for the second division: which is to say: He is infinite from some sides and finite from the rest of the sides. That too is invalid by two aspects: The first: that the proof we mentioned on the impossibility of an infinite extension stands, whether it is said that He is infinite from all sides or from some sides. The second: that the side which is assumed to be infinite, and the side which is assumed to be finite, either are equal in reality and essence, or are not. As for the first case, it necessitates that it be valid for each one of these two
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a proof (برهان) presented by Imam Razi to establish that Allah cannot be confined to a direction or place (حيز وجهة). The proof is structured as a division (تقسيم) of possibilities and a refutation of each. The author begins by stating the thesis: if Allah were confined to a direction, He would necessarily fall into one of three mutually exclusive cases: (1) infinite from all sides, (2) infinite from some sides and finite from others, or (3) finite from all sides. He then declares all three divisions invalid, so the original claim is false. The bulk of the passage refutes the first two divisions.

For the first division (infinite from all sides), the author gives three proof-wajh (وجوه). The first is a geometrical argument: assume an infinite line and a finite line parallel to it, then rotate the finite line to become aligned (مسامتة) with the infinite one. This would require a first point of alignment on the infinite line, but an infinite line has no first point because above any point there is another. This contradiction proves the impossibility of an infinite extension. The second wajh is a meta-argument: if infinite extension were possible, the proof that the world is finite would collapse, but that proof is accepted by consensus. The third wajh is a theological absurdity: if Allah were infinite in all directions, nothing would be free of His essence, implying mixture with impurities—which no rational person accepts.

For the second division (infinite from some sides, finite from others), the author gives two aspects (وجهان). The first repeats that the proof against infinite extension applies regardless of whether it is from all sides or only some. The second (which is incomplete in the text) considers whether the infinite and finite sides are equal in essence or not; if equal, then the finite would share the property of the infinite (i.e., be infinite as well), which is a contradiction. The text cuts off here, but the conclusion is implied.

The author's argument is rigorous, using logical division, geometrical reasoning, and theological consequences. The proof demonstrates that attributing spatial properties to Allah leads to absurdities, thereby defending divine transcendence (تنزيه).

جهة
حيز
غير متناه
متناه
مسامتة
نقطة أول المسامتة
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'infinite' in this proof refers to Allah's absolute infinity in essence, which would be impossible to refute.
Correction: Imam Razi is not referring to Allah's essential infinity but to a potentially infinite extended magnitude, which is a different concept. The proof shows that such a magnitude is logically impossible.

Checkpoint
In the first geometric argument against the first division, what contradiction arises from assuming an infinite line and a finite line becoming aligned?
A) The finite line cannot move because the infinite line blocks it.
B) There would need to be a first point of alignment on the infinite line, but an infinite line has no first point.
C) The infinite line would have to be finite for alignment to occur.
D) The finite line would also become infinite due to the alignment.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's geometric argument demonstrates that an infinite extended magnitude is logically impossible, thereby refuting the notion that Allah could be confined to a direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The proof shows that the alternative (Allah confined to a direction) leads to absurdities like mixing with impurities. Is there any area of your belief or practice where you, knowingly or unknowingly, limit Allah to a finite concept? What step will you take tonight to purify your tawhid from such limits?
?
If the world is finite and Allah is not bound by place, then your existence is entirely contingent on His will. How does this truth change the way you approach a problem you are facing right now—something you've been treating as if it were out of His control?

Proof of the Impossibility of Infinite Extension
Al-Razi proves that an infinite line is impossible via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi argues that an infinite physical extension is impossible, and the logical principle that whatever leads to a contradiction is itself impossible.

Core Idea
An infinite extension leads to a contradiction, so it cannot exist.

This lesson examines al-Razi's concise proof that an infinite line is impossible. The argument relies on a logical principle: if assuming something leads to an impossibility, then that something is itself impossible. By understanding this proof, you will see how theologians used rational arguments to establish that creation must have a finite beginning, pointing to the Creator's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: 'musamatat' (alignment) and 'bu'd ghayr mutanahi' (infinite extension). Try to follow the logical flow.
The passage is very short but dense.
2
Understand the proof structure
The argument begins with a premise about alignment (musamatat) and non-occurrence (la yahsal). Then it states that this impossibility follows from assuming an infinite line, so the assumption is impossible.
3
Connect to the principle
Identify the logical principle used: if an assumption leads to impossibility, the assumption itself is impossible. This is a form of reductio ad absurdum.
4
Consider the broader context
Ask yourself: How does this proof relate to Islamic theology? It denies the possibility of an infinite physical world, establishing that the universe must have a beginning.
This supports the argument for a Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسامتة ، وأن لا يحصل . وهذا المحال إنما لزم من فرضنا أن ذلك الخط غير متناه ، فوجب أن يكون ذلك محالا . فثبت : أن القول بوجود بعد غير متناه : محال
Alignment, and that it does not occur. This impossibility only followed from our assuming that line is infinite, so it is necessary that that is impossible. So it is established: that the statement of the existence of an infinite extension is impossible.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (burhan) that an infinite extension (bu'd ghayr mutanahi) is impossible. The argument begins from a premise about alignment (musamatat) and non-occurrence, concluding that the assumption of an infinite line leads to an impossibility, so the existence of such an extension is itself impossible. The argument relies on the principle that whatever leads to an impossibility is itself impossible.

Key Terms
بعد غير متناه
محال
مسامتة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think infinite extension is mathematically possible and thus applicable to physical reality.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument targets physical extension, not mathematical abstraction. In Islamic theology, an actual infinite physical entity is impossible because it would lead to logical contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, what is the consequence of assuming an infinite line?
A) It is possible
B) It leads to an impossibility
C) It is necessary
D) It depends

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi proves that an infinite physical extension is impossible because it leads to a logical contradiction, establishing that the universe must be finite and have a beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
If the impossibility of an infinite extension is established, then the universe must have a Creator who is without beginning. How does this change the way you view your accountability today? Are your actions aligned with the fact that you will meet the Eternal One?
