Second Argument: Impossibility of Infinite Distance
al-Razi argues that if infinite distance were not impossible, proof of world's finitude would fail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's second argument for the impossibility of infinite distance, and how it relies on a reductio and consensus.

Core Idea
If infinite distance were possible, no proof of the world's finitude could stand.

Al-Razi presents his second proof that infinite extension is impossible. He argues by reductio: if infinite distance were not impossible, then the proof that the world is finite would fail—but the world's finitude is established by rational consensus. Therefore, the premise must be false. This lesson unpacks the logical structure and the role of consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if...then...'.
The phrase 'ليس مالا' is a textual corruption; it should read 'ليس محالا' (not impossible).
2
Identify the logical structure
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum. It shows that assuming infinite extension leads to an impossible consequence.
The consequence is that the proof of the world's finitude would be unestablishable.
3
Understand the role of consensus
By 'consensus' (ijma'), al-Razi means rational consensus—the fact that all rational people agree the world is finite. This consensus is the standard by which the consequence is deemed false.
This is not merely scholarly consensus but a universal rational judgment.
4
Appreciate the argument's force
The argument does not prove infinite extension is contradictory in itself, but that it would undermine a known truth. This is a common method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : هو أنه إذا كان القول بوجود بعد غير متناه ليس مالا ، فعند هذا لا يمكن إقامة الدليل على أن العالم متناه بكليته . وذلك باطل ) (۳۱) بالإجماع .
The second aspect: if the statement of the existence of an infinite extension is not impossible, then the proof that the world is finite in its entirety cannot be established. And that is false by consensus.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This is the second proof (wajh) that infinite extension is impossible. It argues by reductio: if infinite distance were not impossible, then the proof of the finitude of the universe would be impossible, but the finitude of the universe is established by consensus (ijma'). Therefore, the premise is false.

Key Terms
بعد غير متناه
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'consensus' here refers only to the agreement of scholars.
Correction: Al-Razi means rational consensus – the universal agreement of all rational minds on the finitude of the world.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, what follows if infinite extension were not impossible?
A) The world would be infinite
B) The proof of the world's finitude would be impossible to establish
C) God would be omnipresent
D) All things would be finite

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's second argument shows that denying the impossibility of infinite distance leads to the collapse of any proof for the world's finitude, which is impossible by rational consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe the world is finite, but have you ever taken ownership of the rational proof for that belief, or are you just repeating what you've been told? This lesson shows that your conviction has a logical spine—are you willing to trace its bones yourself, or do you prefer intellectual hand-me-downs?
?
If you were to entertain the possibility that anything—like infinite distance—could be possible, what else in your worldview would collapse? This lesson forces you to see that some impossibilities are necessary for truth to hang together. What are you afraid to say is absolutely impossible?
?
Al-Razi stakes the entire argument on rational consensus. Do you have the humility to submit your private opinions to the reasoned agreement of thoughtful minds across generations, or do you cling to comfortable doubts to avoid the burden of certainty? Your answer will show whether you are a seeker of truth or a guardian of convenience.

The Absurdity of God Being Infinite in All Directions
Al-Razi refutes infinite spatial extension of God via reductio

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi rejects the notion that God is infinite in all directions through a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Core Idea
If God were infinite in all directions, impurities would mix with His essence—an absurdity.

Al-Razi presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum to safeguard divine transcendence. He argues that attributing infinite physical extension to God leads to impossible consequences that no rational person would accept. This lesson examines that argument and its implications for tanzih (transcendence).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then... and then...'.
The passage is concise but dense.
2
Understand the conditional premise
Identify the premise: if God were infinite from all sides, then no direction or space would be devoid of His essence.
3
Grasp the absurd consequence
The consequence: the world and even impurities would be mixed with God's essence. This is rationally impossible.
This is the core of the reductio.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Reflect on how this argument protects God's transcendence from physical contamination.
Al-Razi uses logical impossibility to affirm divine tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث : إنه لو كان (تعالى) غير متناه من جميع الجوانب، وجب أن لا يخلو شيء من الجهات والأحياز عن ذاته، وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون العالم مخالطا بأجزاء (۳۳) ذاته ، وأن تكون القاذورات والنجاسات · كذلك ، وهذا لا يقوله عاقل
The third aspect: if He (exalted) were infinite from all sides, it would be necessary that nothing of directions and spaces be devoid of His essence, and then it would follow that the world is intermixed with parts of His essence, and that filths and impurities are likewise, and no rational person says this.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This argument refutes the notion that God is infinite in all directions. If that were the case, then no direction or space would be empty of His essence, leading to the absurd conclusion that the material world, including impurities, would be mixed with God's essence. Since this is rationally unacceptable, the premise is false.

Key Terms
غير متناه
ذات
جهات
أحياز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this argument denies God's omnipresence or knowledge of all things.
Correction: The argument only denies physical presence in space, not God's all-encompassing knowledge or power.

Checkpoint
What would follow if God were infinite in all directions?
A) He would be everywhere in knowledge
B) The world would be mixed with His essence
C) He would be beyond space
D) He would be finite

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's argument shows that attributing infinite spatial extension to God leads to absurdities, affirming His absolute transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If God's essence is not mixed with the world, then your connection to Him is not physical proximity. Are you relying on a false sense of closeness based on location? How can you strengthen your awareness of His real presence—through knowledge and obedience?

Refutation of Partial Divine Infinity
Al-Razi refutes the claim that God is infinite from some sides and finite from others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the view that Allah is infinite from some sides and finite from others is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
A being partially infinite and partially finite is contradictory and composite.

Al-Razi continues his critique by addressing a more nuanced claim: that God might be infinite in some directions but finite in others. He shows that this too collapses into absurdity, either by the same proof against infinite extension or by leading to composition or change in the divine essence. This lesson walks through the two main arguments he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two-part structure: 'two aspects' and then 'several aspects' within the second.
2
Identify the two main proofs
The first proof is a repetition of the earlier argument that infinite extension is impossible regardless of whether it is from all sides or some sides. The second proof is more detailed and examines whether the infinite and finite sides are equal or different in reality.
The second proof branches into two sub-cases.
3
Understand the case where sides are equal
If the infinite and finite sides are equal in reality and quiddity, then they could swap, implying change in Allah — which is impossible. Also it implies separation and conjunction, which is absurd.
This shows that the supposed partial infinity leads to unacceptable consequences.
4
Understand the case where sides are different
If the sides are different in reality, then Allah's essence would be composite (murakkab). Moreover, all spatial objects are equal in being extended, so differentiation in sides is impossible. This also leads to impossibility.
This argument relies on the nature of spatial objects (mutahayyiz).
5
Reflect on the overall conclusion
Both branches of the second proof lead to impossibility. Thus the claim that Allah is partially infinite is false. This reinforces the absolute transcendence of Allah from any spatial or quantitative attributes.
This lesson connects to the broader theme of divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال : إنه غير متناه من بعض الجوائب ومتناه من سائر الجوانب . فهو أيضا باطل من وجهين : الأول : إن البرهان الذي ذكرناه على امتناع بعد غير متناه : قائم . سواء ( كان قد ) قيل : إنه غير متناه من كل الجوانب ، أو من بعض الجوانب . الثاني : إن الجانب الذي فرض أنه غير متناه ، والجانب الذي فرض متناه . إما أن يكونا متساويين في الحقيقة والماهية ، وإما أن لا يكونا كذلك . أما القسم الأول فإنه يقتضي أن يصح على كل واحد من هذين الجانبين ، ما صح على الجانب الآخر . وذلك يقتضي أن ينقلب الجانب المتناهي غير متناه والجانب الغير المتناهي متناهيا . وذلك يقتضي جواز الفصل والوصل والزيادة والنقصان في ذات الله تعالى . وهو محال . وأما القسم الثاني - وهو القول بأن أحد الجانبين مخالف للجانب الثاني في الحقيقة والماهية - فنقول : إن هذا محال من وجوه : الأول : إن هذا يقتضي كون ذاته مركبا . وهو باطل لما بينا . الثاني : إنا بينا أنه لا معنى للمتحيز إلا الشيء الممتد في الجهات المختص بالأحياز . وبينا أن المقدار يمتنع أن يكون صفة ، بل يجب أن يكون ذاتا . وبينا أنه متى كان الأمر كذلك كان جميع المتحيزات متساوية ، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع القول بأن أحد جانبي ذلك الشيء مخالف للجانب الآخر في الحقيقة والماهية.
As for the second division: that He is infinite from some sides and finite from the other sides. It is also invalid from two aspects: The first: the proof we mentioned on the impossibility of an infinite extension stands whether it is said that He is infinite from all sides or from some sides. The second: the side assumed infinite and the side assumed finite, either they are equal in reality and quiddity, or not. As for the first case, it requires that each of these two sides be valid for the other side. That requires that the finite side becomes infinite and the infinite side becomes finite. That requires the possibility of separation and conjunction and increase and decrease in the essence of God Almighty. That is impossible. As for the second case - the statement that one side is different from the other in reality and quiddity - we say: this is impossible from several aspects: The first: this necessitates His essence being composite, which is invalid as we explained. The second: we explained that there is no meaning of occupying space except a thing extended in directions and particular to spaces. And we explained that quantity cannot be an attribute, but must be an essence. And we explained that when it is like that, all occupying-space things are equal. And when it is like that, it is impossible to say that one side of that thing is different from the other side in reality and quiddity.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage refutes the view that God is infinite in some directions and finite in others. The first proof repeats the earlier argument that infinite extension is impossible regardless. The second proof is more detailed: if the infinite and finite sides are equal in reality, then they could swap, implying change in God. If they are different, then God's essence would be composite. Further, all spatial objects are equal in being extended, so differentiation in sides is impossible. Thus the view is false.

Key Terms
متناه
غير متناه
حقيقة
ماهية
مركب
متحيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God is infinite in some directions, He can still be simple because directions are not part of His essence.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that any spatial differentiation leads to composition or change, which is incompatible with divine simplicity.

Checkpoint
What does the second proof argue if the two sides of God are different in reality?
A) They can still be infinite
B) God's essence would be composite
C) God would be finite
D) Sides are irrelevant

Key Takeaway
Allah cannot be described as partially infinite without contradiction, as it leads to change or composition in His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's mercy and His justice, do you unconsciously imagine one attribute as 'bigger' or more 'active' than the other? Al-Razi's argument shows that any division of God's essence leads to contradiction. How can you train your heart to see all of Allah's attributes as equally infinite and inseparable from His essence? Will you repent of any mental image that reduces Him to parts?
?
This refutation leaves no room for thinking that Allah is limited in any way. Yet, do you find yourself limiting Him in your du'a or expectations? What specific area of your life do you need to expand your trust in His absolute power today?
?
The proof shows that partial infinity leads to change or composition in Allah. Have you ever felt that Allah's response to you 'changed' based on your deeds? How does this truth about His unchanging essence affect your relationship with Him? Will you ask Him to help you see Him as He truly is?

Refuting Divine Finitude: Two Proofs from al-Razi
Al-Razi presents two proofs against God's finitude from all sides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's two rational arguments against the claim that God is finite from all sides, and why finitude entails createdness and spatial limitations incompatible with divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Finitude implies contingency and empty spaces—neither can apply to Allah.

Al-Razi continues his systematic refutation of anthropomorphic views, now addressing the claim that God is finite from all directions. He presents two concise rational proofs that such finitude would entail characteristics of contingent beings, which cannot apply to the Creator. This passage strengthens the foundation of divine transcendence by eliminating any conceptual limitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the structure: al-Razi introduces the third division and then gives two numbered proofs.
The passage is concise but packed with logical reasoning.
2
Identify the two proofs
Locate the two arguments: (1) everything finite is susceptible to increase/decrease, hence created (hadith); (2) if finite, there would be empty spaces above Him, contradicting His being above all.
The first proof relies on the principle that contingent objects can change; the second on spatial implications.
3
Reflect on the logical implications
Why does susceptibility to increase/decrease indicate createdness? How does the possibility of empty spaces invalidate divine finitude? Think about the attributes of God that these proofs protect.
These proofs underscore God's necessity and absolute transcendence over space.
4
Connect to broader kalam theology
Understand that this argument is part of a larger tradition defending God's incomparability. The point is that any physical attribute would necessitate contingency.
Al-Razi's method here is typical of later kalam: using rational proofs to eliminate false attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث : - وهو أن يقال : إنه متناه من كل الجوانب -. فهذا أيضا باطل من وجهين : الأول : إن كل ما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب ، كانت حقيقته قابلة للزيادة والنقصان ، وكل ما كان كذلك ، كان محدثا . على ما بيناه . الثاني : إنه لما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب ، فحينئذ يفرض فوقه أحياز خالية ، وجهات فارغة ، فلا يكون ( الله ) (٢٦) تعالى فوق جميع العالم.
As for the third division - that He is finite from all sides - this is also invalid from two aspects: The first: everything that is finite from all sides, its reality is susceptible to increase and decrease, and everything like that is created (hadith), as we have explained. The second: since it is finite from all sides, then empty spaces and vacant directions are supposed above it, so God (exalted) is not above all the world.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage refutes the view that God is finite in all directions. Two proofs: first, anything finite can be increased or decreased, indicating it is contingent and created (hadith). Second, if God is finite, there would be empty spaces beyond Him, contradicting His being above all things.

Key Terms
متناه

أحياز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God can be conceptually limited like a physical object, e.g., having a specific size or location.
Correction: The passage shows that any limitation would imply change (and thus createdness) or spatial surroundings, both impossible for God.

Checkpoint

A) Because finite things are composite
B) Because finite things are susceptible to increase/decrease
C) Because finite things exist in time
D) Because finite things are contingent

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi demonstrates that claiming God is finite from all sides leads to absurdities: either God is created (due to changeability) or He is not above everything (due to empty spaces), both of which are false for the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If Allah were finite, there would be empty spaces above Him. In your life, what 'empty spaces' have you created—gaps where you feel Allah is not present? How does this passage call you to fill those gaps with the awareness that He encompasses everything?

Refutation of the Three Possibilities for God's Relation to Directions
Razi refutes three possible ways a body could relate to directions to show Allah cannot be in one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Allah is in a direction leads to three impossible possibilities, and how each is refuted.

Core Idea
If Allah were in a direction, three contradictions follow, proving His transcendence.

Imam Razi presents a powerful logical argument to disprove the notion that Allah could occupy a direction or space. He systematically examines every possible way a body could relate to directions and shows each leads to absurdity. This lesson walks through his three-part disproof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the complete Arabic passage carefully, noting the three divisions. Then read the translation.
The argument is dense; read slowly.
2
Map the three possibilities
Identify the three possible ways a body could relate to directions if Allah were in one. Notice how Razi labels them with القسم الأول, الثاني, الثالث.
These correspond to: both infinite, one finite one infinite, both finite.
3
Analyze each refutation
For each possibility, note the specific logical contradiction Razi identifies. Ask yourself why each contradiction is impossible for Allah.
The refutations build on earlier principles.
4
Understand the overall conclusion
After refuting all three possibilities, Razi concludes that the original claim is impossible. Grasp how the disjunctive syllogism works here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجانبين، ما صح على الجانب الآخر. وذلك يقتضي أن ينقلب الجانب المتناهي غير متناه والجانب غير المتناهي متناهيا. وذلك يقتضي أو الفصل والوصل والزيادة والنقصان في ذات الله تعالى. وهو محال. وأما القسم الثاني - وهو القول بأن أحد الجانبين مخالف للجانب الثاني في الحقيقة والماهية - فنقول: إن هذا محال من وجوه: الأول: إن هذا يقتضي كون ذاته مركبا. وهو باطل لما بينا. الثاني: إنا بينا أنه لا معنى للمتحيز إلا الشيء الممتد في الجهات المختص بالأحياز. وبينا أن المقدار يمتنع أن يكون صفة، بل يجب أن يكون ذاتا. وبينا أنه متى كان الأمر كذلك كان جميع المتحيزات متساوية، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع القول بأن أحد جانبي ذلك الشيء مخالف للجانب الآخر في الحقيقة والماهية. وأما القسم الثالث: - وهو أن يقال: إنه متناه من كل الجوانب - فهذا أيضا باطل من وجهين: الأول: إن كل ما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب، كانت حقيقته قابلة للزيادة والنقصان، وكل ما كان كذلك، كان محدثا. على ما بيناه. الثاني: إنه لما كان متناهيا من جميع الجوانب، فحينئذ يفرض فوقه أحياز خالية، وجهات فارغة، فلا يكون الله تعالى فوق جميع الأشياء، بل تكون تلك الأحياز أشد فوقية من الله تعالى. وأيضا: فهو تعالى قادر على خلق الجسم في الحيز الفارغ، فلو فرض حيز خال، لكان قادرا على أن يخلق فيه جسما. وعلى هذا التقدير يكون ذلك الجسم فوق الله تعالى. وذلك عند الخصم محال. فثبت: أنه تعالى لو كان في جهة، لم يخل الأمر من أحد هذه الأقسام الثلاثة، وثبت أن كل واحد منها باطل محال، فكان القول بأن الله تعالى في الحيز والجهة، محالا.
The two sides, what is valid for one side is valid for the other. That requires that the finite side become infinite and the infinite side become finite. That requires separation or connection and increase or decrease in the essence of God, which is impossible. As for the second division—which is the statement that one of the two sides differs from the other side in reality and essence—we say: this is impossible in several respects: First, it would require His essence to be composite, which is false as we have shown. Second, we have shown that there is no meaning of being located (al-mutahayyiz) except a thing extended in directions and occupying spaces. We have shown that magnitude cannot be an attribute but must be an essence. And we have shown that if this is so, then all located things are equal, and if so, it is impossible to say that one side of that thing differs from the other side in reality and essence. As for the third division—which is to say that it is finite from all sides—this too is false on two counts: First, whatever is finite from all sides, its reality is susceptible to increase and decrease, and whatever is like that is created, as we have shown. Second, when it is finite from all sides, then above it are presumed empty spaces and vacant directions, so God would not be above all things, but rather those spaces would be more above than God. Also, He is powerful to create a body in the empty space; if an empty space is assumed, He would be able to create a body in it. On this supposition, that body would be above God. That is impossible for the opponent. So it is established: if He were in a direction, the matter would not escape from one of these three divisions, and it is established that each one of them is false and impossible. So the statement that God is in space and direction is impossible.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a proof (argument) refuting the claim that Allah exists in a direction. Razi presents a disjunctive argument: if Allah were in a direction, then concerning His relation to that direction, one of three possibilities must hold: either both sides of His essence are infinite in that direction (i.e., extend beyond the direction), or one side is finite and the other infinite, or both sides are finite. He then shows each case leads to an impossible consequence. For the first case (both sides infinite), it would require that the finite side becomes infinite and vice versa, implying change in Allah's essence. For the second case (one side finite, the other infinite), he argues that this would make Allah's essence composite (since the two sides differ in reality) and also contradicts the nature of located bodies which are all equal (thus no side can differ in essence). For the third case (both sides finite), he gives two sub-arguments: finitude implies susceptibility to increase/decrease, which is a mark of creation; and finitude would allow empty spaces above Allah, making them 'more above' than Him, and even allow a created body to be above Him, which is absurd. Thus all three possibilities are impossible, so the original claim is false. The conclusion is that Allah cannot be in a direction or space.

حيز
متناه
لا متناه
متحيز
ذات
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God being 'non-finite' means He is spatially infinite.
Correction: The first possibility shows that even spatial infinity leads to contradiction (change in essence).

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the third possibility regarding Allah's relation to directions, and why is it impossible?
A) It is impossible because it would make Allah composite.
B) It is impossible because finitude implies susceptibility to increase/decrease and would allow something above Allah.
C) It is impossible because it requires the sides of Allah to be equal.
D) It is impossible because it would make Allah's essence change.

Key Takeaway
Allah's transcendence means He is not in any direction or space, as demonstrated by the impossibility of all logical possibilities.

?

?
Razi's proof shows that finitude is a mark of creation. Have you ever, even unwittingly, thought of Allah as having some kind of limit? What will you do today to actively remind yourself of His absolute transcendence and infinitude in your worship?

The Two Meanings of 'Non-Finite' (غير متناه)
Razi answers an objection by distinguishing two meanings of 'non-finite'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's distinction between two meanings of 'non-finite' and how it defends Ash'ari theology from a crucial objection.

Core Idea
God's infinity is not spatial or directional; it is being unbounded by any direction.

Razi addresses an apparent inconsistency: if Ash'aris claim God is infinite, why do they reject the infinite regress in the physical universe? He shows that 'infinite' has two senses. One applies to God (no direction or place), the other applies to imagined infinite extension in space. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the Ash'ari position on divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note how the opponent tries to turn the Ash'ari argument against them.
The objection is a classic tu quoque (you too) argument.
2
Identify the two meanings
Razi explicitly lists two meanings of 'non-finite'. Find them and note the key difference: being free from direction vs. being within a direction but unlimited.
The first meaning is about Allah; the second about imagined spatial extension.
3
See how Razi resolves the objection
Razi shows that if the opponent means the first meaning, there is no dispute. If they mean the second, the proof against infinite regress applies to them, not to Ash'aris.
The argument only works if the opponent insists on the second meaning.
4
Apply the distinction
Test your understanding with the checkpoint. Then try the activity to articulate the distinction in your own words.
This distinction is a core Ash'ari move to protect divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: ألستم تقولون: إنه تعالى غير متناه في ذاته، فيلزمكم جميع ما ألزمتموه علينا؟ قلنا: الشيء الذي يقال له: إنه غير متناه على وجهين: أحدهما: إنه غير مختص بحيز وجهة. ومتى كان كذلك، امتنع أن يكون له طرف ونهاية وحد. والثاني: إنه مختص بجهة وحيز، إلا أنه مع ذلك ليس لذاته مقطع وحد. فنحن إذا قلنا: إنه لا نهاية لذات الله تعالى عنينا به التفسير الأول. فإن كان مرادكم ذلك، فقد ارتفع الخلاف بيننا، وإن كان مرادكم هذا الوجه الثاني، فحينئذ يتوجه عليكم ما ذكرناه من الدليل، ولا ينقلب ذلك علينا لأن لا نقول إنه تعالى غير متناه - بهذا التفسير - حتى يلزمكم ذلك الإلزام. فظهر الفرق. والله أعلم.
If it is said: Do you not say that He, exalted, is non-finite in His essence, so that all you have required of us would be incumbent upon you? We say: The thing of which it is said that it is non-finite is of two types: one of them is that it is not particularized by a direction and space. And if it is so, it is impossible for it to have an extremity, an end, or a limit. The second is that it is particularized by a direction and space, except that nevertheless its essence does not have an extremity or limit. So when we say that there is no end to the essence of God, we mean by it the first interpretation. If you mean that, then the disagreement between us is removed. But if you mean this second type, then what we have mentioned of the proof applies to you, and it does not turn back upon us because we do not say that He, exalted, is non-finite according to this interpretation, so that that requirement would be incumbent upon you. Thus the difference is clear. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent raises an objection: 'You (the Ash'aris) claim that Allah is non-finite (lā nihāya) in His essence. Then by your own argument, if God is non-finite, He would be like the first possibility you rejected (both sides infinite), and thus the same refutation would apply to you.' Razi responds by clarifying that 'non-finite' has two meanings. The first meaning is that something is not particularized by any direction or space, and thus it cannot have an extremity or limit at all—this is the meaning when applied to Allah. The second meaning is that something is particularized by a direction and space, but its essence has no specific cut-off or limit (e.g., an infinite spatial extension). Razi states that their claim about Allah uses the first meaning, not the second. If the opponent also means the first, then there is no disagreement. If they mean the second, then the earlier proof applies to them, not to the Ash'aris, because the Ash'aris do not affirm that Allah is non-finite in the second sense. Thus the objection is answered.

Key Terms
غير متناه
ذات
جهة
حيز
تفسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'non-finite' necessarily implies infinite spatial extension.
Correction: Razi distinguishes two meanings: the first is being free from direction/space (applicable to God), and the second is infinite extension in a direction (not applicable to God).

Checkpoint
What is the first meaning of 'non-finite' (غير متناه) according to Razi?
A) Being extended without limit in a direction.
B) Being particularized by a direction but without limit.
C) Not being particularized by any direction or space.
D) Having an endless duration.

Key Takeaway
Razi clarifies that God's infinity means He is unbounded by any direction, not that He is infinitely extended in space.

The Fourth Proof: Impossibility of Necessary Existence in a Direction
Razi presents a fourth proof that Allah cannot be in a direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's fourth proof that the Necessary Existence cannot exist in a direction or space, and why both logical possibilities are impossible.

Core Idea
Allah cannot be in a direction because both necessary and contingent spatial existence are impossible for Him.

Razi continues to establish divine transcendence by showing that even the notion of Allah occupying a direction leads to rational absurdities. In this brief but powerful argument, he lays out a disjunction that eliminates any possibility of Allah being confined to space. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the concise structure of the proof.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Razi presents a conditional statement: if Allah were in a direction, then either His existence there is necessary or not necessary. Identify both parts.
These are the two branches of the disjunction.
3
Understand why each possibility is impossible
Reflect on why both options are impossible for the Necessary Existent. Necessary spatial existence ties Allah to a contingent place; non-necessary spatial existence implies change and contingency.
The commentary provides explanation.
4
Recognize the conclusion
Since both possibilities are false, the original assumption (that Allah is in a direction) must be false. This is a proof by contradiction.
The statement 'the claim that Allah exists in a direction is impossible' is the conclusion.
5
Apply the lesson to divine transcendence
Consider how this proof fits into the broader Islamic doctrine that Allah is transcendent and not confined by space or direction.
This is a key part of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الرابع على أنه يمتنع أن يحصل في الجهة والحيز: هو أنه لو حصل في شيء من الجهات والأحياز، لكان إما أن يحصل مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه، أو لا مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه. والقسمان باطلان، فكان القول بأنه تعالى حاصل في الجهة محالا.
The fourth proof that it is impossible for Him to exist in a direction and space is: if He existed in any of the directions and spaces, then He would either exist with necessity of existence in it, or not with necessity of existence in it. And both divisions are false, so the statement that He, exalted, exists in a direction is impossible.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a proof (argument) that Allah cannot exist in a direction or space. Razi presents a simple disjunction: if Allah were to exist in a particular direction or space, then His existence in that place would either be necessary (i.e., He must be there) or not necessary (i.e., He could be elsewhere). Both options are impossible. The first option (necessary existence in that place) would imply that the place is inseparable from Allah and perhaps eternal, which is impossible for a contingent place. The second option (not necessary) would imply that Allah can exist in different places, which would entail change and contingency, also impossible for Allah. Therefore, the claim that Allah exists in a direction is false. The proof is concise and relies on the impossibility of either necessity or contingency of place for the Necessary Existent.

Key Terms
برهان
جهة
حيز
وجوب
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God is omnipresent, He must be in every direction.
Correction: This proof shows that even being in one direction is impossible for Allah. Omnipresence in Islamic theology means His knowledge and power encompass all, not that His essence is spatially spread.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's fourth proof, if Allah were in a direction, what are the two possibilities?
A) That He is there by His essence or by His power.
B) That He is there with necessity or without necessity.
C) That He is there eternally or temporarily.
D) That He is there in one direction or in all directions.

Key Takeaway
Razi's fourth proof establishes that the Necessary Existence cannot be in a direction because doing so would entail either necessary or contingent spatial existence, both of which are impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believe Allah is not in any direction, how does that change the way you feel His closeness when you pray? Does your heart need to adjust what it means to be 'near' to Allah?
?
When you recite 'Allahu Akbar' and raise your hands, are you subconsciously pointing toward a direction? Pledge to yourself today to reaffirm in your heart that Allah is beyond all directions.

Conclusion of the Third Proof: God Cannot Be in a Direction
Imam al-Razi concludes the third proof against God being in a direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses a reductio argument to prove that God cannot be in a direction, specifically the absurdity of a body being above God.

Core Idea
If God were in a direction, something could be above Him—an impossibility.

This passage concludes the third proof. Al-Razi presents a hypothetical scenario that the opponent cannot accept: if there were an empty space above God, God could create a body there, placing that body above Him. Since this is impossible, the assumption that God is in a direction must be false. The argument relies on the opponent's own commitment to 'above-ness' for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: a hypothetical scenario followed by a conclusion.
2
Identify the hypothetical and its impossibility
Find the part where al-Razi imagines an empty space above God. Understand why the opponent must accept that God could create a body there, making that body 'above' God—something the opponent deems impossible.
This is the core of the reductio: the assumption leads to an unacceptable consequence.
3
Understand the overall logical structure
Recognize that this is a reductio ad absurdum: from the assumption 'God is in a direction' comes one of three impossible consequences (only one is stated here). Since all three are impossible, the assumption is false.
The argument does not require enumerating the other two consequences; it suffices that one is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأشياء، بل تكون تلك الأحياز أشد فوقية من الله تعالى. وأيضاً: فهو تعالى قادر على خلق الجسم في الحيز الفارغ، فلو فرض حيز خال، لكان قادراً على أن يخلق فيه جسماً. وعلى هذا التقدير يكون ذلك الجسم فوق الله تعالى. وذلك عند الخصم محال. فثبت: أنه تعالى لو كان في جهة، لم يخل الأمر من أحد هذه الأقسام الثلاثة، وثبت أن كل واحد منها باطل محال، فكان القول بأن الله تعالى في الحيز والجهة، محالا.
Things, rather those spaces would be more above than God Almighty. And also: He Almighty is able to create the body in the empty space, so if an empty space is assumed, He would be able to create a body in it. On this estimation that body would be above God Almighty. And that is impossible according to the opponent. So it is established: that if He Almighty were in a direction, the matter would not be free from one of these three divisions, and it is established that each one of them is false and impossible, so the statement that God Almighty is in space and direction is impossible.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is the concluding part of a proof by contradiction. It first presents one of the three impossible consequences of claiming God is in a direction: if there were an empty space above God, He could create a body there, which would then be above Him—this is unacceptable to the opponent who holds that nothing is above God. It then states that the assumption of God being in a direction necessarily leads to one of three divisions (presumably enumerated earlier), all of which are proven impossible. Therefore, the claim is false. The argument relies on the opponent's own premise that God is above all.

Key Terms
جهة
حيز
فوقية
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a proof from physical space, assuming the existence of empty space above God.
Correction: No, it is a reductio ad absurdum that derives an impossibility from the opponent's own view that God is in a direction and that nothing is above Him. It does not assert the actual existence of empty space; it is a hypothetical.

Checkpoint
What impossible consequence does Imam al-Razi present in this passage if God were in a direction?
A) God would be divisible.
B) A body could be created above God.
C) God would have a body.
D) God would be in multiple directions.

Key Takeaway
The assumption that God is in a direction leads to absurd consequences, proving that God transcends all direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe God is beyond all direction, how would that change the way you pray? Would you still feel God is 'above' in the sky? What would you need to replace that image with?
?

?

The Two Meanings of Infinite
Al-Razi responds to the objection by distinguishing two meanings of 'infinite'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses a distinction between two meanings of 'infinite' to defend divine transcendence from the charge of entailment.

Core Idea
God's infinity means not being confined to space, not having no end.

The objector tries to turn al-Razi's own argument against him: if you say God is infinite, do you not face the same problems you accuse us of? Al-Razi shows that the objection equivocates on the word 'infinite'. He distinguishes a meaning that applies to God from one that would entail the difficulties. This distinction is a powerful tool in kalām.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objector's challenge: 'Do you not say God is infinite? Then the same problems apply to you.' Get the sense of it before analyzing.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Al-Razi says 'the thing said to be infinite is of two kinds'. Find each kind and see how he defines them. The first: not specific to space/direction. The second: specific but without a cut or boundary.
The first meaning is about non-confinement; the second is about lack of an end within a confined thing.
3
See which interpretation al-Razi accepts for God
Al-Razi explicitly says he means the first interpretation when saying God is infinite. The second interpretation is what the objector would have to intend for the objection to work, but al-Razi denies that of God.
4
Understand how this refutes the objection
If the objector also means the first interpretation, then there is no disagreement. If the objector means the second, then the proof al-Razi gave earlier applies to them, not to him. So the objection is neutralized.
This is a classic move against equivocation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: ألستم تقولون: إنه تعالى غير متناه في ذاته، فيلزمكم جميع ما ألزمتموه علينا؟ قلنا: الشيء الذي يقال له: إنه غير متناه على وجهين: أحدهما: إنه غير مختص بحيز وجهة. ومتى كان كذلك، امتنع أن يكون له طرف ونهاية وحد. والثاني: إنه مختص بجهة وحيز، إلا أنه مع ذلك ليس لذاته مقطع وحد. فنحن إذا قلنا: إنه لا نهاية لذات الله تعالى عنينا به التفسير الأول. فإن كان مرادكم ذلك، فقد ارتفع الخلاف بيننا، وإن كان مرادكم هذا الوجه الثاني، فحينئذ يتوجه عليكم ما ذكرناه من الدليل، ولا ينقلب ذلك علينا لأنّا لا نقول إنه تعالى غير متناه - بهذا التفسير - حق [؟] ياز [؟] مناذلك [؟] الإلزام فظهر الفرق. والله أعلم.
If it is said: Do you not say that He Almighty is infinite in His essence, so the same objections you bring against us apply to you? We say: The thing that is said to be infinite is of two kinds: one: it is not specific to space and direction. And when it is such, it is impossible that it have an extremity and limit and boundary. And the second: it is specific to a direction and space, except that despite that its essence has no cut and boundary. So we, when we say that there is no limit to the essence of God Almighty, we mean by it the first interpretation. If you mean that, then the disagreement between us is removed; but if you mean this second kind, then the proof we mentioned applies to you, and it does not turn back on us, because we do not say that He Almighty is infinite — according to this interpretation — right [؟] [unclear] the objection [؟]; so the difference appears. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This is an objection and answer. The objector alleges that if Razi holds God to be infinite, the same problems (of having a direction, etc.) would apply. Razi responds by distinguishing two meanings of 'infinite'. The first meaning is that which is not confined to space or direction and has no limit; this applies to God. The second meaning is that which is confined but without an end; Razi denies this of God. Thus the objection fails because it equivocates on the term 'infinite'. The garbled final sentence likely reinforces that the objection does not apply.

Key Terms
غير متناه
جهة
حيز
نهاية
حد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'infinite' always means 'having no end in a given direction', implying spatial extension.
Correction: Al-Razi clarifies that another meaning is 'not being confined to any direction at all', which is how God is infinite.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, which meaning of 'infinite' does he affirm for God?
A) Infinite in time and infinite in space.
B) Not specific to any space or direction.
C) Specific to a direction but without an end.
D) Both meanings simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defends divine transcendence by showing that God's infinity means independence from space and direction, not endless extension within them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God's infinity, do you catch yourself thinking of a limitless expanse in space? How does today's lesson reveal that as a subtle form of limiting God? What would it look like to purify your heart from that image?
?
The objector assumed that 'infinite' must mean the same for God as for physical things. Where in your own life have you assumed that God is bound by the same categories as creation? Ask yourself: Do I secretly think God needs a place to dwell, or that He moves from one place to another? What does that say about my understanding of His transcendence?
?
Al-Razi says God is infinite in the sense of being free from space and direction. If you truly believed that God is not 'up' or 'down' but beyond all directions, how would it change the way you pray? Would you still feel the need to face a direction, or would you experience a deeper closeness that transcends orientation?

The Fourth Proof: Main Division and First Argument
Division and first argument against necessary location

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main division of the fourth proof against God being in a direction and the first argument based on equality of essences.

Core Idea
Necessary location leads to equality with bodies, which is impossible for God.

This lesson introduces the fourth proof that God cannot be in a direction. Imam al-Razi begins by dividing the assumption into two possibilities: either God is in a direction necessarily or not necessarily. He then focuses on the first possibility and presents the first argument against it, using the principle that if God were necessarily in a direction, His essence would be equal to bodies, leading to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of division and argument.
The first line states the overall proof and division.
2
Identify the main division
Find the two possibilities presented. Understand why both are considered false by the author.
The division is: necessary location or not necessary location.
3
Analyze the first argument
Trace the logic: equality of essences → full equality → validity transfer → contradiction.
This argument relies on the principle of equality established earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الرابع على أنه يمتنع أن يحصل في الجهة والحيز: هو أنه لو حصل في شيء من الجهات والأحياز، لكان إما أن يحصل مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه، أو لا مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه. والقسمان باطلان، فكان القول بأنه تعالى حاصل في الجهة محالاً.

وإنما قلنا: إنه يمتنع أن يحصل فيه مع الوجوب (وهذا هو القسم الأول) لوجوه:

الأول: إن ذاته مساوية لذوات سائر الأجسام في كونه حاصلاً في الحيز، ممتداً في الجهة. وإذا ثبت التساوي من هذا الوجه، ثبت التساوي في تمام الذات، على ما بيناه في البرهان الأول في نفي كونه تعالى جسماً. وإذا ثبت التساوي مطلقاً، فكل ما صح على أحد المتساويين وجب أن يصح على الآخر. ولما لم يجب في سائر الذوات حصولها في ذلك الحيز، وجب أن لا يجب في تلك الذوات حصولها في ذلك الحيز. وهو المطلوب.

الثاني: إنه لو وجب حصوله في تلك الجهة، وامتنع حصوله في سائر الجهات، لكانت تلك الجهة مخالفة في الماهية لسائر الجهات، وحينئذ تكون الجهات شيئاً موجوداً. فإذا كان الله سبحانه وتعالى واجب الحصول في الجهة أزلاً وأبداً، التزموا قديماً آخر مع الله تعالى في الأزل، وذلك محال.

الثالث: لو جاز في شيء مختص بجهة معينة أن يقال: إن اختصاصه بتلك الجهة واجب، جاز أيضاً ادعاء أن بعض الأجسام حصل في حيز معين على سبيل الوجوب، بحيث يمتنع خروجه عنه. وعلى هذا التقدير لا يتمشى دليل حدوث الأجسام في ذلك. فثبت: أن القائل بهذا القول لا يمكنه الجزم بحدوث كل الأجسام، بل يلزمه تجويز أن يكون بعضها قديماً.

الرابع: هو أنا نعلم بالضرورة: أن الأحياز بأسرها متساوية، لأنها فراغ محض، خلاء صرف. وإذا كانت بأسرها متساوية يكون حكمها
The fourth proof that it is impossible for Him to be in direction and space: It is that if He were in some direction or space, He would be either with necessity of being in it, or not with necessity of being in it. And both divisions are false, so the statement that He Almighty is in a direction is impossible.

And we say: It is impossible for Him to be in it with necessity (and this is the first division) for reasons:

First: His essence is equal to the essences of all other bodies in being in space, extended in direction. And if equality is established from this aspect, equality is established in the entire essence, as we explained in the first proof negating that He Almighty is a body. And if equality is established absolutely, then everything that is valid for one of the two equals must be valid for the other. Since the other essences are not necessarily in that space, it must be that they are not necessarily in that space. And that is what is required.

Second: If His being in that direction were necessary, and His being in other directions were impossible, then that direction would be different in quiddity from other directions, and then directions would be existent things. So if God Almighty is necessarily in a direction eternally and forever, they would have committed to another eternal being with God in eternity, and that is impossible.

Third: If it could be said of something specific to a particular direction that its specificity to that direction is necessary, it would also be permissible to claim that some body is in a specific space by way of necessity, such that its removal from it is impossible. On this estimation, the proof of the temporal creation of bodies would not hold. So it is established that the one who says this cannot be certain of the temporal creation of all bodies, but rather he must allow that some of them are eternal.

Fourth: We know necessarily that spaces as a whole are equal, because they are pure vacuum, empty void. And if they are as a whole equal, their judgment is...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof against God being in a direction, structured as a division. The proof states: if God were in a direction, either He is necessarily in it or not. Both are impossible. The text focuses on refuting the first case (necessity) with four arguments. The first argument uses the principle of equality: God's essence would be equal to bodies in being in space, leading to absurdities. The second argues that necessary location would make the direction an eternal entity, implying another eternal besides God. The third undermines the proof of the world's temporal origination by allowing eternal bodies. The fourth (incomplete) argues that all spaces are equal, so no reason for necessity. The second division (not necessary) is not discussed here.

Key Terms
البرهان الرابع
وجوب
تساوي
حيز
جهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that necessary location is possible if God's essence is different from bodies.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that equality in being in space implies equality in essence, leading to absurdities.

Checkpoint
What are the two divisions in the fourth proof against God being in a direction?
A) Either God is in a direction necessarily or not necessarily.
B) Either God is in a direction eternally or temporarily.
C) Either God is in a direction by choice or by nature.
D) Either God is in a direction or He is not.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof uses a division to show that necessary location is impossible, starting with an argument from equality of essences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you ever subconsciously imagine God as being in a certain direction (e.g., above the heavens)? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what will you do to correct your mental image of God?
?
This argument shows that assuming God is in a direction leads to logical absurdities. In your daily life, do you ever attribute to God limitations that are only applicable to created beings? Reflect on one specific belief you held that this lesson corrects, and commit to internalizing the truth of His transcendence.
?
The principle of equality is used here to deny necessary location. Are you willing to follow logical arguments about God even when they contradict your emotional or traditional attachments? What is one attachment you need to let go of after this lesson?

The Fourth Proof: Second, Third, and Fourth Arguments
Three arguments against necessary location: second, third, and incomplete fourth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three additional arguments that refute the necessity of God being in a direction: the argument from multiplicity of eternals, the argument from undermining temporal origination, and the argument from equality of spaces.

Core Idea
Necessary location would imply another eternal, undermine proof of creation, and contradict spatial equality.

This lesson continues the fourth proof by examining the remaining arguments against the necessity of God being in a direction. Imam al-Razi presents three further arguments: the second shows it would lead to another eternal, the third undermines the proof of temporal creation, and the fourth argues from the equality of all spaces. Note that the fourth argument is incomplete in the source.

Guided Path
1
Read each argument separately
Read the second argument, then the third, then the incomplete fourth. Understand each one's logic.
The second and third are complete; the fourth ends mid-sentence.
2
Analyze the second argument
Focus on the idea that a necessary location would make that direction an eternal entity, implying another eternal with God.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the third argument
Understand how allowing necessary location would permit some bodies to be eternal, undermining the proof of temporal origination.
This argument defends the cosmological proof.
4
Examine the fourth argument
Note that spaces are all equal; if they are equal, no reason for necessity. The source ends here, but the argument is clear.
Equality of spaces implies no one space is special.

Source Text

وإنما قلنا: إنه يمتنع أن يحصل فيه مع الوجوب (وهذا هو القسم الأول) لوجوه:

Divine Transcendence

First Proof: Equality of Bodies Denies Divine Corporeality
Al-Razi presents the first proof that God cannot necessarily occupy space.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's first rational proof that God cannot necessarily occupy a specific space, based on the equality of all bodies in being located in space.

Core Idea
If all bodies are equal in being in space, then none can be necessarily tied to a particular space.

Al-Razi begins his demonstration of God's transcendence by addressing the claim that God might necessarily occupy a particular space. He offers a proof based on the logical implications of equality among bodies. This argument, which relies on an earlier proof that God is not a body, is a cornerstone of rational theology. Let's examine how it works.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully and then the translation. Note the logical structure and identify the key terms for space, direction, equality, and body.
Pay attention to the phrase 'مساواة' (equality) which is central.
2
Identify the key premises
Find the three main claims: equality in being located in space and extended in direction, equality in the entire essence, and the transfer of necessity from one equal to the other.
Al-Razi references an earlier proof that God is not a body to support the step from partial equality to full equality.
3
Understand the conclusion
See how Al-Razi uses the false necessity for other bodies to deny necessity for God. Since no other body is necessarily in a particular space, God cannot be necessarily in one either.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يحصل فيه مع الوجوب ( وهذا هو القسم الأول ) لوجوه : الأول : إن ذاته مساوية لذوات سائر الأجسام في كونه حاصلا في الحيز . ممتدا فى الجهة . وإذا ثبت التساوى من هذا الوجه ، ثبت النساوى في تمام الذات . على ما بيناه فى البرهان الأول في نفي كونه تعالى جسما . و إذا ثبت التساوى مطلقاً ، فكل ما صح على أحد المتساويين وجب أن يصح على الآخر . ولما لم يجب فى سائر الذوات حصولها في ذلك الحيز ، وجب أن لا يجب في تلك الذوات حصولها في ذلك الحيز . وهو المطلوب
We say: It is impossible for Him to occur in space with necessity (and this is the first division) for reasons: First: His essence is equal to the essences of all other bodies in being located in space, extended in direction. When equality is established in this respect, equality is established in the entire essence, as we explained in the first proof negating that He is a body. When equality is established absolutely, then whatever is correct for one of the two equals must be correct for the other. Since it is not necessary for the other essences to be located in that space, it is necessary that it is not necessary for those essences to be located in that space. That is what is sought.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage contains the first argument against the claim that God necessarily occupies a particular space. Al-Razi begins by stating the impossibility of God being in space necessarily (the first division). He then presents the proof: God's essence is comparable to all other bodies in terms of being located in space and extended in direction. If equality holds in this respect, then equality holds in the entire essence. Since all bodies are equal, if one body were necessarily in a space, all would be, which is false. Therefore, it is not necessary for any body to be in that specific space, so God cannot be necessarily in space. This proof relies on the earlier demonstration that God is not a body.

Key Terms
حيز (space)
جهة (direction)
مساواة (equality)
جسم (body)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because God is unique, He cannot be compared to other bodies in any way.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that in terms of being located in space and extended in direction, God's essence is equal to other bodies, and therefore the same logical rules apply.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the first proof that God cannot necessarily occupy space?
A) God's essence is unique and incomparable.
B) All bodies are equal in being located in space, so necessity cannot single out one.
C) Space is eternal and God is eternal, so they must coincide.
D) The proof relies on revelation, not reason.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's first proof uses the equality of all bodies in being located in space to show that no body, including God's, can be necessarily tied to a particular space.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read Al-Razi's argument that God cannot be necessarily tied to any space. Reflect on your own times of worship—have you ever felt that God is 'closer' in the mosque or during salah? Does this argument challenge your assumption that God is 'present' in certain places? How will you now cultivate awareness of God's presence without limiting Him to a space?
?
The proof uses equality among bodies to deny necessity of location for God. In your daily life, do you treat certain people as if they are 'more worthy' of God's nearness? How does the equality of all bodies in being located in space remind you that God is equally near to all, without being confined?
?
Al-Razi's logical argument strips away any notion that God is tied to a place. How does this affect your understanding of du'a? Do you ever think God only hears when you are in a specific place? What will you change about your prayer habits knowing that God is not bound by spaces?

The Danger of Attributing Direction to Allah
Al-Razi's second proof against God having direction by reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Razi argues that attributing a necessary direction to Allah leads to the impossibility of multiple eternal beings.

Core Idea
If God is necessarily in a direction, that direction must be co-eternal with God.

Al-Razi presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum: if God were necessarily located in a specific direction, that direction would have to be a distinct, eternal entity alongside Him. This would contradict the fundamental Islamic belief in the oneness of the Eternal. Let's examine this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let Al-Razi's own words set the stage for the logical reasoning.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if ... then ...'.
2
Identify the premise
Al-Razi starts with a conditional: if God's occurrence in a specific direction were necessary and impossible elsewhere, then that direction differs in essence from others.
This is the foundation of the argument.
3
Trace the implication
From that difference in essence, Al-Razi infers that directions are something existent (not mere mental constructs).
4
Reach the conclusion
Since God is eternal and always in that direction, the direction itself would be eternal alongside God, leading to multiple eternal beings.
This is the absurd conclusion that refutes the premise.
5
Reflect on the impossibility
Multiple eternal beings is impossible (muhal) because it violates tawhid. Therefore, the original assumption that God is necessarily in a direction is false.
This ties directly to divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إنه لو وجب حصوله في تلك الجهة ، وامتنع حصوله في سائر الجهات ، لكانت تلك الجهه مخالفة فى الماهية لسائر الجهات ، وحينئذ تكون الجهات شيئاً موجوداً . فإذا كان الله سبحانه وتعالى واجب الحصول في الجهة أزلا وأبداً : التزموا قديماً آخر مع الله تعالى في الأزل وذلك محال
Second: If His occurrence in that direction were necessary and His occurrence in other directions impossible, then that direction would be different in essence from other directions, and then directions would be something existent. So if God is necessarily in that direction eternally and forever, they would be committed to another eternal being with God in pre-eternity, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This is the second argument. Al-Razi reasons: if God necessarily occupies a specific direction, that direction must have a distinct essence from other directions. This implies that directions are real, existent things. Since God is eternally in that direction, the direction itself would be co-eternal with God, leading to multiple eternal beings. But this is impossible because it contradicts the oneness of the Eternal.

Key Terms
جهة (direction)
قديم (eternal)
ماهية (essence)
محال (impossible)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that directions are merely mental constructs and have no real existence, so God being in a direction is harmless.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that if God were necessarily in one specific direction, that direction would have a distinct essence and therefore be a real entity, leading to co-eternal beings.

Checkpoint
What undesirable consequence follows if God necessarily occupies a specific direction?
A) God would be limited in power.
B) That direction would become a second eternal being.
C) God would be subject to change.
D) Directions would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi refutes the necessity of direction by showing it leads to multiple eternal beings, which contradicts the oneness of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself mentally placing Allah 'up above' or 'out there'? How does Al-Razi's proof confront that subtle assumption, and what does that tell you about the way you imagine your Lord?
?
The argument shows that even an unexamined thought about Allah's direction leads to impossible consequences. What other hidden assumptions about Allah might you hold that need to be purified according to the Quran and Sunnah?
?
If Allah is not bound by any direction, then He is equally near to you in every place. Does your worship reflect that reality, or do you still act as if He is distant? What will you change today to live in constant awareness of His closeness?

The Third Proof: Necessary Direction Allows Eternal Bodies
Al-Razi's third proof: necessary location would allow some bodies to be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's third proof that permitting necessary specification to a direction for any thing would undermine the proof that all bodies are temporal.

Core Idea
If a body can be necessarily in a place, then not all bodies need be temporal.

Al-Razi presents a logical argument that exposes a fatal consequence of allowing necessary direction. If the opponent claims that something can be necessarily fixed in a direction, then the same logic could apply to bodies, making some potentially eternal. This destroys the standard argument for the temporality of all bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
The OCR has a typo 'حيز مين' – it should be 'حيز معين' (specific space).
2
Identify the hypothesis
The hypothesis is that it is permissible for something to be said to have necessary specification to a particular direction.
3
Understand the consequence
From that hypothesis, it follows that some bodies could be in a specific space necessarily, and their departure is impossible.
This would mean those bodies are not subject to change in location.
4
See the impact on the temporality proof
The standard proof for temporality of bodies relies on change (e.g., motion). If some bodies are necessarily fixed, the proof does not apply to them.
Hence the opponent cannot claim certainty that all bodies are temporal.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Al-Razi concludes that the opponent must admit the possibility that some bodies are eternal.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو جاز فى شىء مختص بجهة معينة أن يقال : إن اختصاصه بتلك الجهة : واجب ، جاز أيضاً : إدعاء أن بعض الأجسام حصل في حيز مين على سبيل الوجوب ، بحيث يمتنع خروجه عنه . وعلى هذا التقدير لا يتمشى دليل حدوث الأجسام فى ذلك . فثبت : أن القائل بهذا القول، لا يمكنه الجزم بحدوث كل الأجسام ، بل يلزمه تجويز أن يكون بعضها قديماً .
Third: If it were permissible for something specified with a particular direction to be said: its specification to that direction is necessary, then it would also be permissible to claim that some bodies have occurred in a specific space necessarily, such that its departure from it is impossible. On this assumption, the proof of the temporality of bodies would not work. So it is established that the claimant of this statement cannot be certain of the temporality of all bodies; rather, he must allow that some of them may be eternal.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
The third argument shows that allowing necessary specification of direction would undermine the standard proof for the creation of bodies. The typical proof for the temporality of bodies relies on the possibility of change and motion. If some bodies could be necessarily fixed in a place, they could be eternal, and the argument would not apply to all bodies. Thus, the opponent cannot maintain the temporality of all bodies.

Key Terms
اختصاص (specification)
جهة (direction)
حدوث (temporality)
قدم (eternity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that only God can be necessarily located, and that this does not affect arguments about the temporality of bodies.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that if necessary direction is allowed for anything, the same logic applies to bodies, which would undermine the proof that all bodies are temporal.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi argue is a consequence of allowing necessary specification to a direction?
A) All bodies become eternal.
B) The proof of temporality of bodies becomes inapplicable to all bodies.
C) God becomes corporeal.
D) Directions become unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
Allowing necessary direction for any thing makes the standard proof for temporal creation universally invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a particular argument for God's existence is foolproof, without examining its premises? How does Al-Razi's warning challenge your confidence in your own reasoning about the divine?
?
In your own life, do you tend to think that your current state or situation is necessarily fixed, as if you cannot change? How does the lesson's insight about necessary direction exposing the limitations of proofs apply to your own assumptions about change and growth?
?
The opponent in this argument was convinced of his position, but Al-Razi shows it leads to an unacceptable consequence. Are there beliefs you hold that you have never examined for their implications? Commit today to scrutinize one deeply held conviction.

The Fourth Proof: Equality of All Spaces
Al-Razi states the fourth proof that all spaces are equal, precluding necessary specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that all spaces are equal as pure voids, so God cannot be necessarily located in any particular space.

Core Idea
All spaces are identical voids, so none is more fitting for God.

Al-Razi presents his fourth and most developed argument against spatial location for God. He asserts that we know necessarily that all spaces are equal because they are pure vacuum. Therefore, no space can have a special claim to contain the Divine. This lesson examines the core proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the claim and the reason.
2
Understand the premise
Al-Razi says we know necessarily that all spaces are equal. Why? Because they are pure void.
This is an intuitive knowledge.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Since all spaces are equal, it is impossible for God to be necessarily attached to a specific one.
The conclusion is a direct negation of the corporealist view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع، هو أنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن الاحيان بأسرها متساوية . لأنها فراغ محض ، خلاء صرف . وإذا كانت بأسرها متساوية يكون حكمها واحداً . وذلك يمنع من القول بأنه تعالى واجب الاختصاص ببعض الأحياز على التعيين. فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يكون اختصاصه بجهة فوق : أولى ؟ قلنا : هذا باطل لوجوه : أحدها : إن قبل خلق العالم، ما كان إلا الخلاء الصرف والعدم المحض. فلم يكن هناك فوق ولا تحت . فيطل قولكم . الثانى : إنه لو كان الفوق متميزاً عن التحت بالتميز الذاتي ، لكانت الجهات أمورا موجودة ممتدة قابلة للانقسام وذلك يقتضى تقدم الجسم. لأنه لا معنى للجسم إلا ذلك : الثالث : هو أنه لو جاز أن تختص ذات الإله تعالى ببعض الجهات على سبيل الوجوب مع كون الأحياز متساوية في العقل ، لجاز اختصاص بعض الحوادث المعينة ببعض الأوقات دون البعض على سبيل الوجوب ، مع كونها متساوية في العقل . وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم استغناؤها عن الصانع ، ولجاز أيضاً اختصاص عدم القديم ببعض الأوقات على سبيل الوجوب . وعلى هذا التقدير ينسد باب إثبات مصانع ، وباب إثبات وجوبه وقدمه
Fourth: We know necessarily that all spaces are equal, because they are pure vacuum, absolute void. If they are all equal, their judgment is one. That prevents saying that He is necessarily specified with some spaces determinately. If they say: Why is it not permissible that His specification to the direction of above be more appropriate? We say: This is false for reasons: One: Before the creation of the world, there was only pure void and absolute nothingness. So there was no above or below. So your statement becomes false. Second: If above were distinct from below by essential distinction, then directions would be existent things, extended, divisible, and that would necessitate the priority of body, because body means nothing but that. Third: If it were permissible for the essence of God to be specified to some directions by way of necessity while spaces are equal in reason, then it would be permissible for some particular events to be specified to some times rather than others by way of necessity while they are equal in reason. On this assumption, their independence from the Maker would be necessary, and it would also be permissible for the non-existence of the Eternal to be specified to some times by way of necessity. On this assumption, the door of proving the Maker is closed, and the door of proving His necessity and pre-eternity is closed.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This is the fourth and most elaborate argument. Al-Razi asserts that we know necessarily that all spaces (ahiyaz) are equal because they are pure vacuum. Therefore, none can be more appropriate for God. He then anticipates an objection: why not say the 'above' direction is more appropriate? He refutes this with three sub-arguments. First, before creation there was no above or below, so the distinction is not inherent. Second, if above and below were essentially distinct, directions would be real extended entities, which would imply body, contradicting God's incorporeality. Third, if necessary specification is allowed despite equality, then similar logic would apply to times, allowing events to be necessary without a Maker, and even allowing the non-existence of the Eternal to be fixed in time, which would undermine the proofs for God's existence and eternity.

Key Terms
حيز (space)
فراغ (vacuum)
خلاء (void)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'above' is a special direction even before creation.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that spaces are identical, so no direction is special by nature.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi say about the nature of spaces?
A) They are physical objects.
B) They are pure void.
C) They are created.
D) They are relative.

Key Takeaway
All spaces are equal as pure vacuum, so God cannot be necessarily located in any one space.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you unconsciously imagine God in a specific direction, like above the heavens? How does this argument challenge that tendency, and what steps can you take to purify your tawheed from spatial concepts?
?
If all spaces are equal voids, then no physical place is holier than another in terms of containing God. Yet you still face the Kaaba in prayer. How do you reconcile this act of direction with the truth that God is not confined to any space? Does your heart truly accept that God is beyond all directions?

First Refutation: The Absence of Directions Before Creation
Al-Razi gives the first rebuttal against specifying God with 'above'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's first argument that before creation there was no 'above' or 'below', so 'above' cannot be inherently superior.

Core Idea
Before the world, there was no direction, so 'above' is not eternal.

The corporealist might object that the 'above' direction is more appropriate for God. Al-Razi begins his refutation by pointing out that before the creation of the world, there was only void and nothingness, so concepts like 'above' and 'below' did not exist. Therefore, they cannot be eternal attributes of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first refutation
Read the Arabic text of the objection and Al-Razi's first answer.
2
Analyze the premise
Al-Razi says before creation, only pure void and absolute nothing existed. Therefore, above and below were not real.
This undermines the claim that 'above' is inherently special.
3
Draw the conclusion
If above and below only came into being with creation, they cannot be necessary attributes of God.
This refutes the objection.

Second Refutation: Directions as Extended Entities Imply Body
Al-Razi's second argument shows that essential distinction of directions would entail body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's second argument that if 'above' and 'below' were essentially distinct, they would be extended divisible entities, which would imply body, contradicting God's incorporeality.

Core Idea
If 'above' and 'below' were real, they'd be physical, making God a body.

Al-Razi's second refutation goes deeper. If the directions 'above' and 'below' were inherently distinct, they would have to be real extended things that can be divided. But that is exactly the definition of a body. If God were located in such a direction, He would be in a bodily place, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the second refutation
Read the Arabic text of the second argument.
2
Understand the conditional
If above and below were essentially distinct, they would be existing, extended, and divisible.
This is a hypothetical.
3
Connect to body
Extended divisible existence is the definition of body, so that would mean directions are bodies, and God's location would imply body.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
