Third Refutation: The Slippery Slope to Atheism
Al-Razi's third argument shows the absurd consequences of allowing necessary specification despite equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's third argument that allowing necessary specification for God despite equality of spaces would lead to allowing necessary specification of events in time, which would eliminate the need for a Creator and undermine proofs of God's existence and eternity.

Core Idea
If God can be fixed in space, then events can be fixed in time without a cause.

Al-Razi's third refutation is a compelling reductio ad absurdum. He argues that if we allow that God is necessarily specified to a direction even though all spaces are equal, then we should also allow that particular events are necessarily specified to particular times even though all times are equal. This would abolish the need for a Creator and even allow the non-existence of the Eternal to be fixed in time, which destroys all proofs for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the third refutation
Read the Arabic text of the third argument. It is a longer passage.
2
Understand the analogy
Al-Razi draws an analogy: spaces are equal, times are equal. If necessary specification is allowed for God in space, then it should be allowed for events in time.
This is a logical parallel.
3
See the consequences
If events are necessarily specified to times, they would be independent of a Maker. Also, the non-existence of the Eternal could be specified to a time, which is absurd.
This closes the door to proving God's existence and eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع، هو أنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن الاحيان بأسرها متساوية . لأنها فراغ محض ، خلاء صرف . وإذا كانت بأسرها متساوية يكون حكمها واحداً . وذلك يمنع من القول بأنه تعالى واجب الاختصاص ببعض الأحياز على التعيين. فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يكون اختصاصه بجهة فوق : أولى ؟ قلنا : هذا باطل لوجوه : أحدها : إن قبل خلق العالم، ما كان إلا الخلاء الصرف والعدم المحض. فلم يكن هناك فوق ولا تحت . فيطل قولكم . الثانى : إنه لو كان الفوق متميزاً عن التحت بالتميز الذاتي ، لكانت الجهات أمورا موجودة ممتدة قابلة للانقسام وذلك يقتضى تقدم الجسم. لأنه لا معنى للجسم إلا ذلك : الثالث : هو أنه لو جاز أن تختص ذات الإله تعالى ببعض الجهات على سبيل الوجوب مع كون الأحياز متساوية في العقل ، لجاز اختصاص بعض الحوادث المعينة ببعض الأوقات دون البعض على سبيل الوجوب ، مع كونها متساوية في العقل . وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم استغناؤها عن الصانع ، ولجاز أيضاً اختصاص عدم القديم ببعض الأوقات على سبيل الوجوب . وعلى هذا التقدير ينسد باب إثبات مصانع ، وباب إثبات وجوبه وقدمه
Fourth: We know necessarily that all spaces are equal, because they are pure vacuum, absolute void. If they are all equal, their judgment is one. Third: If it were permissible for the essence of God to be specified to some directions by way of necessity while spaces are equal in reason, then it would be permissible for some particular events to be specified to some times rather than others by way of necessity while they are equal in reason. On this assumption, their independence from the Maker would be necessary, and it would also be permissible for the non-existence of the Eternal to be specified to some times by way of necessity. On this assumption, the door of proving the Maker is closed, and the door of proving His necessity and pre-eternity is closed.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This is the fourth and most elaborate argument. Al-Razi asserts that we know necessarily that all spaces (ahiyaz) are equal because they are pure vacuum. Therefore, none can be more appropriate for God. He then anticipates an objection: why not say the 'above' direction is more appropriate? He refutes this with three sub-arguments. First, before creation there was no above or below, so the distinction is not inherent. Second, if above and below were essentially distinct, directions would be real extended entities, which would imply body, contradicting God's incorporeality. Third, if necessary specification is allowed despite equality, then similar logic would apply to times, allowing events to be necessary without a Maker, and even allowing the non-existence of the Eternal to be fixed in time, which would undermine the proofs for God's existence and eternity.

Key Terms
حيز (space)
وقت (time)
وجوب (necessity)
صانع (Maker)
قديم (Eternal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think necessary specification is harmless.
Correction: Al-Razi shows it leads to a chain of absurdities that undermine all theistic proofs.

Checkpoint
What is the ultimate consequence of allowing necessary specification for God in space?
A) It proves God is above.
B) It closes the door to proving God's existence and eternity.
C) It shows God is everywhere.
D) It confirms the need for a Maker.

Key Takeaway
If necessary spatial specification is allowed, then similar temporal specification would make proofs for God impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever acted as if your circumstances (time, place, upbringing) necessarily determine your choices, rather than your own free will? How does that mentality undermine your sense of responsibility before God?
?
If you truly believe that God's existence is necessary and not subject to time or space, why do you sometimes feel distant from Him or doubt His reality? Could it be that you are unconsciously treating God as contingent like other things?
?
When you face a difficult decision, do you ever feel that there is no real choice — that 'it was meant to be' or 'it had to happen'? How does the lesson's rejection of necessary temporal specification challenge that feeling and call you to embrace genuine moral responsibility?

The Paralytic Analogy: Why God Cannot Be Confined to Space
Al-Razi presents the fifth proof comparing necessary location to a paralytic or bound being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's fifth proof that God cannot be necessarily located in space, using the analogy of a paralytic or bound being.

Core Idea
Necessary location would make God like a paralytic — a deficiency impossible for Him.

Al-Razi introduces his fifth argument against God's spatial location. He draws a striking analogy: if God were necessarily confined to a specific space without the power to leave, He would resemble a helpless paralytic or a captive. Such limitation implies deficiency, which is impossible for the perfect Creator. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice the concise style and the analogical structure.
The passage is short but packs a logical punch.
2
Identify the analogy
Al-Razi uses two comparisons: a paralytic and a bound person. What do they have in common? Both lack the ability to move from their current state.
The key is 'cannot exit' – necessary location means inability to leave.
3
Understand why this is a deficiency
If God cannot leave a space, He is limited and dependent on that space. This contradicts His perfection and omnipotence.
Deficiency (naqṣ) is impossible for God.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
This proof supports tanzīh – that God is beyond space and direction, free from all creaturely limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: إنه لو حصل فى حيز معين - مع أنه لا يمكنه الخروج - لكان كالمفلوج الذى لا يمكنه أن يتحرك ، أو كالمربوط الممنوع عن الحركة . وكل ذلك نقص، والنقص على الله مجال .
Fourth [actually fifth]: If He were to occur in a specific space – while He cannot exit it – He would be like the paralytic who cannot move, or like the tied one prevented from movement. All of that is deficiency, and deficiency upon God is impossible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This argument uses an analogy to highlight an absurd consequence. If God necessarily occupies a space and cannot leave it, He would be comparable to a paralytic or a bound person who lacks the ability to move. This implies deficiency and limitation, which cannot be attributed to God, who is perfect and omnipotent. Thus, necessary location is impossible.

Key Terms
حيز (space)
مفلوج (paralytic)
مربوط (tied)
نقص (deficiency)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Being in a place does not necessarily imply inability to move; one could be in a place voluntarily.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument specifically targets necessary location (i.e., God cannot leave), not voluntary location. The inability to exit is the deficiency.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Al-Razi use to show the deficiency of necessary location?
A) A king in his palace.
B) A paralytic or bound person.
C) A stone in its place.
D) A fish in water.

Key Takeaway
God's perfection precludes any limitation, including being necessarily confined to space.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Impossibility of Contingent Location for God
Al-Razi begins the second division by rejecting contingent spatial location for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Razi argues that it is impossible for God to be in space even contingently, because contingency requires a cause for specification.

Core Idea
Contingency does not escape the need for a cause.

In the first division, it was argued that God cannot be necessarily in space. Here, Al-Razi addresses the second possibility: that God could be in space contingently. He shows that this too leads to an impossible conclusion: without a preponderant factor, there is no reason for God to be in one space rather than another.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note that the passage is incomplete but the main argument is clear.
The sentence cuts off, but we understand the principle.
2
Understand the opponent's claim
The opponent concedes God is not necessarily in space but could be contingently. Identify the key term 'جواز' (contingency/permissibility).
3
Grasp Al-Razi's rebuttal
Al-Razi says this is impossible because if location is contingent, there must be a cause (preponderance) to specify which space. Otherwise existence in that space would not be preponderant over non-existence.
The argument relies on the principle of causation.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
This argument shows that God's transcendence is not accidentally but necessarily free from spatial location, because any relation to space would require a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و أما القسم ثاني . وهو أن يقال: إنه تعالى لو حصل في الحيز، مع جواز كونه حاصلا فيه . فنقول: هذا مجال لأنه لو كان كذلك لما ترجح وجود
As for the second division, and that is that it is said: He could occur in space, while it is possible for Him to be in it. We say: This is impossible, because if it were so, [His] existence would not be preponderant
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the second major argument, where the opponent might concede that God is not necessarily in space but could be contingently there. Al-Razi immediately dismisses this as impossible. He argues that if God's location were contingent, there would need to be a preponderant factor to specify one space over others, otherwise existence in that space would not be preponderant over non-existence. The argument is incomplete here, but the logical principle is clear: contingency requires a cause for specification.

Key Terms
قسم ثان (second division)
جواز (contingency/permissibility)
ترجح (preponderance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think contingency avoids the problems of necessity, but Al-Razi points out it leads to an infinite regress or ungrounded choice.
Correction: Contingency requires a cause for specification, which would ultimately regress or be arbitrary, both impossible for God.

Checkpoint
What problem does Al-Razi identify with the claim that God could be in space contingently?
A) It contradicts revelation.
B) It would require a cause to preponderate one space over another.
C) It implies God is limited.
D) It is impossible because space is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi shows that even contingent location for God is impossible because it would require a cause to specify which space, leading to an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever subconsciously limit God by thinking of Him as being 'in heaven' or confined to a place, such that you forget His absolute transcendence? How does Al-Razi's argument force you to reconsider where and how you perceive God's presence?
?
If God is not bound by space, then His closeness to you is not a matter of physical proximity. Are you living as if you can be close to God wherever you are, or do you feel distant when you are not in a 'sacred' place? What would change if you truly believed God is accessible everywhere?
?
The argument shows that every contingent thing needs a cause for its particularity. When you look at your own life—your birth, your circumstances, your choices—do you acknowledge that you are contingent in every detail and utterly dependent on God's preponderant will? Or do you act as if some aspects of your life are self-determined without reference to Him?

Four Arguments Against God's Necessary Direction
Imam Razi refutes the claim with four arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four rational arguments proving that Allah cannot be necessarily confined to any direction, especially 'above'.

Core Idea
Allah is beyond all directions; necessity and location are incompatible.

Imam Razi presents a cascade of arguments to dismantle the claim that Allah is necessarily in a specific direction, like above. These arguments draw on pre-creation, the nature of bodies, the implications for divine self-sufficiency, and the deficiency of confinement. Each argument targets a different aspect of the claim, building a cumulative case for tanzih (transcendence).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the four numbered arguments (أحدها, الثانى, الثالث, الرابع).
2
Examine the first argument
Understand the premise: before creation there was no above or below, so direction cannot be necessary.
This argument uses the temporal priority of void.
3
Examine the second argument
If directions were intrinsically distinct, they would be extended and divisible, implying a body, which cannot be true of Allah.
Body is defined as extended and divisible.
4
Examine the third and fourth arguments
The third argument shows the logical consequence of allowing necessary assignment despite equal options; the fourth shows confinement implies deficiency.
These arguments highlight the implications for divine independence and perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحداً . وذلك يمنع من القول بأنه تعالى واجب الاختصاص ببعض الأحياز على التعيين. فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يكون اختصاصه بجهة فوق : أولى ؟ قلنا : هذا باطل لوجوه : أحدها : إن قبل خلق العالم، ما كان إلا الخلاء الصرف والعدم المحض. فلم يكن هناك فوق ولا تحت . فيطل قولكم . الثانى : إنه لو كان الفوق متميزاً عن التحت بالتميز الذاتي ، لكانت الجهات أمورا موجودة ممتدة قابلة للانقسام وذلك يقتضى تقدم الجسم. لأنه لا معنى للجسم إلا ذلك : الثالث : هو أنه لو جاز أن تختص ذات الإله تعالى ببعض الجهات على سبيل الوجوب كون الأحياز متساوية في العقل ، لجاز اختصاص بعض الحوادث المعينة ببعض الأوقات دون البعض على سبيل الوجوب ، مع كونها متساوية في العقل . وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم استغناؤها عن الصانع ، ولجاز أيضاً اختصاص عدم القديم ببعض الأوقات على سبيل الوجوب . وعلى هذا التقدير ينسد باب إثبات مصانع ، وباب إثبات وجوبه وقدمه الرابع : إنه لو حصل فى حيز معين - مع أنه لا يمكنه الخروج - لكان كالمفلوج الذى لا يمكنه أن يتحرك ، أو كالمربوط الممنوع عن الحركة . وكل ذلك نقص، والنقص على الله تعالى مجال .
One. And that prevents the statement that He, exalted, is necessarily assigned to some specific places. For if they say: Why is it not permissible that His assignment to the direction of above be preferable? We say: This is false for several reasons: First: Before the creation of the world, there was only pure void and absolute nothingness. So there was no above and no below. Thus your statement becomes invalid. Second: If above were distinct from below by an essential distinction, then directions would be existing extended things divisible, and that necessitates the priority of the body. For the meaning of body is nothing but that. Third: If it were permissible for the essence of God, exalted, to be assigned to some directions necessarily while places are equal in reason, then it would be permissible for some specific events to be assigned to some times rather than others necessarily, while they are equal in reason. On this assumption, their independence from the Maker would be necessary, and it would also be permissible for the non-existence of the eternal to be assigned to some times necessarily. On this assumption, the door of proving the Maker and the door of proving His necessity and pre-eternity would be closed. Fourth: If He occurred in a specific place—while He cannot leave—He would be like a paralytic who cannot move, or like one tied and prevented from movement. All that is deficiency, and deficiency upon God, exalted, is impossible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that God occupies direction "above" necessarily. Imam Razi provides four arguments: (1) Before creation, only void existed, so no direction. (2) If directions are distinct in themselves, they'd be extended and divisible, thus bodily. (3) If God's necessary direction were allowed despite equal alternatives, then events could be necessary without a chooser, undermining proofs for the Creator and His pre-eternity. (4) Being confined to a specific place without ability to leave implies impotence and deficiency, which is impossible for God.

Key Terms
واجب الاختصاص
جهة فوق
خلاء صرف
عدم محض
جسم
تقدم الجسم
حادث
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying 'God is above' is a necessary literal attribute.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that direction cannot be necessary for Allah; before creation there was no direction, and direction implies body, so it cannot be an attribute of the Creator.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument against God being necessarily above?
A) Before creation there was no above or below.
B) Directions are bodies.
C) It would lead to events needing no Creator.
D) It implies deficiency.

Key Takeaway
Allah is free from all spatial constraints; any claim of necessary direction is rationally indefensible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Even Possibility Fails: God Cannot Be in Space
Razi proves impossibility even under concessive possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why even if God's being in space were possible, it would still be impossible due to the requirement of a preponderating cause and the implication of temporality.

Core Idea
Possibility does not eliminate the need for a cause—God must be eternal and beyond space.

Imam Razi presents a powerful argument against the possibility of God occupying space. Even if one grants that it is possible, the logic of contingency demands a cause that makes it actual, which would render God's spatiality temporal and thus impossible for the Eternal. Let's examine this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the issue
The passage addresses the second division: even if God's being in space were possible, it is still impossible. Read the Arabic and translation to get the full picture.
2
Follow the causal argument
Razi argues that if God were in space, that situation would require a preponderating cause (agent/specifier). Since the cause precedes the effect, God's being in space would not be eternal.
Notice how possibility itself does not grant actuality.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
If God is eternal and free from space, becoming spatial would mean change in His essence, which is impossible. Connect this to the doctrine of divine transcendence.
This argument reinforces tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و أما القسم الثاني . وهو أن يقال: إنه تعالى لو حصل فى الحيز، مع جواز كونه حاصلا فيه . فنقول: هذا محال لأنه لو كان كذلك لما ترجح وجود ذلك الاختصاص إلا بفعل فاعل، وتخصيص مخصص، وكل ما كان كذلك، فالفاعل يتقدم عليه. فيلزم أن لا يكون حصول ذات الله تعالى فى الحيز أزليا. لأن ما تأخر عن الغير لا يكون أزليا. وإذا كان الأزلي مبرأ عن الوضع والحيز، امتنع أن يصير بعد ذلك مختصا بالحيز، وإلا لزم وقوع الانقلاب فى ذاته تعالى وإنه محال. وبالله التوفيق.
As for the second division: It is that it is said: If He, exalted, occurred in space, while it is possible that He occurs in it. We say: This is impossible, because if it were so, then the existence of that assignment would not be preponderant except by the act of an agent and the specification of a specifier, and everything that is so, the agent precedes it. So it would follow that the occurrence of the essence of God, exalted, in space would not be eternal. For that which is posterior to another is not eternal. And when the Eternal is free from position and space, it is impossible that He becomes after that assigned to space, otherwise change in His essence would occur, and that is impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is the second division: Even if one grants that God could be in space (not necessarily), it is still impossible. The argument: If His being in space is merely possible, it requires a preponderating cause. But the cause must precede the effect. Therefore, God's being in space would be temporal, not eternal. Since God is eternal and free from space, He cannot later become spatial; that would be change in His essence, which is impossible.

Key Terms
حيز
جواز
ترجح
فاعل
مخصص
أزلي
انقلاب الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something is possible, it does not need a cause to exist.
Correction: In Islamic theology, every contingent possibility requires a preponderating cause to bring it from potentiality to actuality.

Checkpoint
Why does God's being in space being possible still lead to impossibility?
A) Because possible things need no cause.
B) Because it would make God temporal.
C) Because space is created.
D) Because above is a direction.

Key Takeaway
Even if God's being in space were possible, the necessity of a preponderating cause would make it temporal, contradicting God's eternal transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Proof from Spherical Earth: God is Not in Space
Imam Razi proves God is not in space using the spherical shape of the earth and lunar eclipses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the spherical shape of the earth and lunar eclipse timing to argue that God cannot be confined to any spatial direction.

Core Idea
Direction is relative on a sphere; God cannot be in a relative direction.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a clever astronomical proof: the earth's sphericity, demonstrated by lunar eclipse observations, shows that concepts like 'above' and 'below' are relative to the observer's location. If God were assigned a direction, He would be 'below' for some people, which is unanimously rejected. Therefore, God transcends spatial dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof structure
The argument has two main parts: first, establishing that the earth is spherical; second, deducing from that that God cannot be in any spatial direction or location.
2
Examine the eclipse argument
Read the lunar eclipse example carefully. Notice how the same event is observed at different local times in the east and west, proving the earth's curved surface.
The eclipse occurs simultaneously, but local time differs.
3
Grasp the relativity of direction
On a sphere, 'above' and 'below' are not absolute. What is up for one observer is down for another. This is key to the proof.
4
Apply to the Creator
If God were in a specific direction, He would be 'below' for some people, which is impossible by consensus. Therefore, God is not confined to space.
Imam Razi mentions agreement between Muslims and opponents on this point.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this proof is powerful: it uses observable phenomena to establish a theological truth about God's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الخامس : هو أن الأرض كرة، وإذا كان كذلك، امتنع كونه تعالى في الحيز والجهة. بيان الأول : إنه إذا حصل خسوف قمري، فإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المشرق عن ابتدائه قالوا: إنه حصل في أول الليل. وإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المغرب قالوا: إنه حصل في آخر الليل. فعلمنا أن أول الليل في أقصى المشرق هو بعينه آخر الليل في أقصى المغرب، وذلك يوجب كون الأرض كرة. وإنما قلنا: إن الأرض لو كانت كرة، امتنع كون الخالق في شيء من الأحياز. وذلك لأن الأرض إذا كانت كرة، فالجهة التي هي فوق بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المشرق هي تحت بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المغرب. وعلى العكس. فلو اختص الباري تعالى بشيء من الجهات، لكان تعالى في جهة التحت بالنسبة إلى بعض الناس، وعلى العكس. وذلك باطل بالاتفاق بيننا وبين الخصم. فثبت أنه يمتنع كونه تعالى مختصا بالجهة.
The fifth proof: That the earth is a sphere, and if it is so, then His being in space and direction is impossible. Explanation of the first: When a lunar eclipse occurs, if we ask the inhabitants of the farthest east about its beginning, they say: It occurred at the beginning of the night. And if we ask the inhabitants of the farthest west, they say: It occurred at the end of the night. So we know that the beginning of the night in the farthest east is exactly the end of the night in the farthest west, and that necessitates that the earth is a sphere. And we say: If the earth is a sphere, then the Creator being in any of the places is impossible. That is because if the earth is a sphere, then the direction that is "above" relative to the inhabitants of the east is "below" relative to the inhabitants of the west, and vice versa. So if the Creator, exalted, were assigned to any direction, He would be in the direction of "below" relative to some people, and vice versa. And that is false by agreement between us and the opponent. So it is established that it is impossible for Him to be assigned to direction.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof: The earth is spherical, as shown by lunar eclipse timing differences between east and west. This implies that direction is relative. If God occupied any direction, He would be below for some people, which is impossible by consensus. Therefore, God is not spatial.

Key Terms
كرة الأرض
خسوف قمري
جهة فوق
جهة تحت
اتفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that 'above' and 'below' are absolute directions in the universe, and that God could be 'above' in a literal spatial sense.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that on a spherical earth, directions are relative. What is 'above' for one observer is 'below' for another. Therefore, God cannot be in any literal spatial direction, as it would lead to contradiction.

Checkpoint
How does the lunar eclipse prove the earth is spherical?
A) It appears at different times in east and west.
B) It appears only at night.
C) It proves the moon orbits the earth.
D) It shows the sun is stationary.

Key Takeaway
God's transcendence of space is proven by the relative nature of directions on a spherical earth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look up at the sky, do you catch yourself imagining Allah as being 'up there' somewhere? How does this proof challenge that mental image, and what will you do to correct it?
?
If directions are relative, then your sense of 'closeness' to Allah cannot be spatial. What does that mean for how you seek His nearness in your daily life?
?
The proof uses a lunar eclipse to show earth's sphericity. Are you willing to let observable evidence shape your understanding of Allah's transcendence, even if it challenges your intuition? Commit to studying more proofs like this.

Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
Impossibility of Allah Being in a Place Due to Temporality
Razi proves that divine location would entail change and temporal posteriority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah cannot occupy a place, based on the argument that location would require an agent, making it temporal and contradicting His eternity, and would also imply change in His essence.

Core Idea
Place would make Allah temporal—impossible for the Eternal.

Razi presents a concise but powerful argument against those who claim Allah occupies a literal location. If Allah were in a place, that location would require a cause; thus it would be temporal, contradicting His eternity. Moreover, acquiring a place after being free of it would imply change in the Divine Essence. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic once slowly, noting the key terms like الحيز and الأزلي. Then read the translation.
Notice the compressed style—every word carries weight.
2
Identify the conditional premise
The argument starts: if Allah were in a place, that specification would require an agent. Why? Because place is not inherent to Allah. Find that reasoning.
The phrase 'إلا بفعل فاعل' indicates necessity of an agent.
3
Follow the conclusion
Trace how Razi moves from 'requires an agent' to 'not eternal' to 'impossible for the Eternal' and finally to 'change is impossible'. The logic is tight.
Also note the second branch: the Eternal free from place cannot later acquire it—that would be change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك الاختصاص إلا بفعل فاعل ، وتخصيص مخصص ، وكل ما كانه كذلك ، فالفاعل يتقدم عليه . فيلزم أن لا يكون حصول ذات الله تعالى فى الخيز أزليا . لأن ما تأخر عن الغير لا يكون أزليا . وإذا كان الأزلي مبرأ عن الوضع والحيز ، امتنع أن يصير بعد ذلك مختصا بالحيز ، وإلا لزم وقوع الانقلاب فى ذاته تعالى و إنه محال
That specification cannot be except by an act of an agent and a particularizing, and everything that is like that, the agent precedes it. So it follows that the existence of the essence of Allah the Exalted in the place is not eternal. Because what is delayed by something else is not eternal. And when the Eternal is free from position and place, it is impossible that thereafter it becomes particularized with the place, otherwise a change in His essence would occur, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an argument proving that Allah cannot be in a place. The author argues that if the divine essence were specified with a place, that specification would require an agent and a particularizer, and since every such specification is preceded by the agent, it would be temporal. But the Eternal cannot be temporal. Moreover, the Eternal is free from place; acquiring a place would constitute a change in His essence, which is impossible. Thus, the initial premise (that Allah is in a place) is false.

Key Terms
الحيز (al-hayyiz: place/space)
الأزلي (al-azalī: the Eternal)
الانقلاب (al-inqilāb: change)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah being 'above' is literal.
Correction: This argument proves any location would make Him dependent on an agent, thus temporal, contradicting His eternity.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is it impossible for Allah to be in a place?
A) Because places are finite and Allah is infinite.
B) Because being in a place would require an agent and thus be temporal, contradicting His eternity.
C) Because the Quran says Allah is not in a place.
D) Because places are created and would limit Him.

Key Takeaway
Razi's argument shows that attributing a place to Allah contradicts His eternity and entails an impossible change in His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you catch yourself imagining Allah in a certain direction or above you? After learning Razi's argument, what concrete step will you take to train your heart to be conscious of Allah without spatializing Him?
?
If your belief about Allah's location was previously vague or anthropomorphic, what must you change in your daily thoughts about Him to align with His transcendence?
?
This proof shows that any place would make Allah dependent on an agent. Have you ever considered how your own existence is dependent and temporal? How should this contrast with the Eternal deepen your urgency to devote your limited time to worshipping Him?

Fifth Proof: Spherical Earth and Divine Direction
Razi uses lunar eclipse observations to prove earth is spherical, then shows God cannot be in a direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the spherical shape of the earth and the relativity of direction to prove that Allah is not confined to any physical direction.

Core Idea
Direction is relative; the Creator cannot be relative.

Razi presents a proof that goes beyond mere theological assertion, using an empirical observation (lunar eclipse) to establish a physical fact (earth is spherical) and then drawing a theological conclusion (God is not in a direction). This lesson walks through each step, showing how reason and observation support divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a very logical structure: first proving the earth's shape, then deducing the theological implication.
2
Understand the First Step
Identify how the lunar eclipse observation proves the earth is a sphere. Why does the time difference matter?
If the earth were flat, the eclipse would be seen at the same time everywhere.
3
Understand the Second Step
Once the earth is spherical, see how directions like 'above' and 'below' become relative. How does this contradict God being in any direction?
If God were 'above' for one person, He would be 'below' for another, which is absurd.
4
Reflect on the Conclusion
Sit with the final conclusion: that Allah is not specified with any direction at all. This is a profound statement about divine transcendence.
This proof does not just deny a specific direction; it denies that God can have any spatial relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الخادس : هو أن الأرض كرة ، وإذا كان كذلك ، امتنع كونه تعالى في الحيز والجهة . بيان الأول : إنه إذا حصل خسوف قمرى ، فإنا إذا سألنا سكان أقصى المشرق عن ابتدائه ؟ قالوا : إنه حصل فى أول الليل . وإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المغرب ؟ قالوا : إنه حصل في آخر الليل . فعلمنا : أن أول الليل في أقصى المشرق ، هو بعينه آخر الليل فى أقصى المغرب ، وذلك يوجب كون الأرض كرة . وإنما قلنا : إن الأرض لو كانت كرة ، امتنع كون الخالق فى شىء من الأحياز . وذلك. لأن الأرض إذا كانت كرة ، فالجهة التي هي فوق بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المشرق ، هى تحت با النسبة إلى سكان المغرب . وعلى العكس . هلو اختص البارى تعالى بشيء من الجهات ، لكان تعالى في جهة التحت. بالنسبة إلى بعض الناس وعلى العكس وذلك باطل بالاتفاق. بيننا وبين الخصم. فثبت : أنه يمتنع كونه تعالى مختصا بالجهة .
The fifth proof: That the earth is a sphere, and if that is the case, then it is impossible for Him (Exalted) to be in place or direction. Explanation of the first: That when a lunar eclipse occurs, if we ask the inhabitants of the extreme East about its beginning, they say: It happened at the beginning of the night. And if we ask the inhabitants of the extreme West, they say: It happened at the end of the night. So we know that the beginning of the night in the extreme East is exactly the end of the night in the extreme West, and that necessitates that the earth is a sphere. And we say: If the earth is a sphere, then it is impossible for the Creator to be in any of the places. That is because if the earth is a sphere, the direction that is 'above' for the inhabitants of the East is 'below' for the inhabitants of the West, and vice versa. So if the Creator (Exalted) were specified with any direction, He would be in a downward direction for some people and the opposite, and that is invalid by agreement between us and the opponent. So it is established that it is impossible for Him (Exalted) to be specified with direction.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof (al-burhān al-khāmis) that Allah cannot be in a place or direction. The proof has two steps: first, it demonstrates that the earth is spherical using the example of a lunar eclipse observed at different times in the East and West. The same eclipse appearing at the beginning of the night in the East and at the end of the night in the West implies that the earth is curved, specifically a sphere. Second, it argues that if the earth is a sphere, then directions like 'above' and 'below' are relative. If Allah were in a specific direction (e.g., above), He would be below for people on the opposite side, leading to a contradiction. Therefore, He cannot be in any direction at all. The proof relies on empirical observation and the relativity of direction.

Key Terms
الخسوف القمري (al-khusūf al-qamarī: lunar eclipse)
الجهة (al-jiha: direction)
الكرة (al-kura: sphere)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'above' is an absolute direction, e.g., that God is literally above the earth.
Correction: This proof shows that 'above' is relative to the observer's position on a spherical earth. What is above for one person is below for another, so God cannot be literally 'above' in any absolute sense.

Checkpoint
How does the lunar eclipse observation prove the earth is a sphere?
A) The eclipse is visible only in the East.
B) The same eclipse is seen at different times in the East and West, indicating the earth is curved.
C) The eclipse lasts longer in the West.
D) The moon appears larger in the East.

Key Takeaway
The spherical earth and the relativity of direction prove that Allah cannot be in any spatial direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah as 'up there' in the sky? This proof shows that even that thought ties Him to a direction that changes depending on where you stand. What would it mean for your worship to truly believe that Allah is beyond all spatial concepts?
?
The proof uses a simple observation—the timing of a lunar eclipse—to unravel a deep theological truth. When you look at the moon, will you now remember that its movement testifies to the absolute transcendence of its Creator? What other everyday signs might you be overlooking?
?
If directions are relative, then your own sense of 'above' is just a local point of view. In your relationship with Allah, where have you been treating your own perspective as absolute, expecting Him to fit into your understanding rather than submitting to His incomparable reality?

The Sixth Proof: Divine Location Implies Similarity to Bodies
Razi presents a proof against Allah being in a place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that if Allah were in a place, He would be a body similar to all bodies, leading to the impossible consequence that either everything is eternal or everything is temporal.

Core Idea
If Allah were in a place, He would be just another body, destroying His uniqueness.

Razi presents a crisp logical proof that Allah cannot occupy space. The argument builds on earlier conclusions about bodies being similar in their essential nature. If Allah were in a place, He would be a body like all others—and that creates an absurdity about eternity and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm, then review the literal translation. Notice the structure: statement, explanation, conclusion.
The proof is called 'al-burhān al-sādis'.
2
Follow the logical steps
Identify the three main steps: (1) If Allah is in a place, He is a body (mutahayyiz). (2) All bodies share the same quiddity. (3) Therefore Allah would be similar to all bodies, implying equal concomitants—leading to absurdity.
Razi references an earlier chapter where the similarity of bodies was established.
3
Understand the impossible consequence
If Allah and all bodies are similar, they must share all properties. Either all are eternal (impossible, since creation is temporal) or all are temporal (impossible, since Allah is eternal). Hence the original assumption is false.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the key terms
Note terms like mutahayyiz (body/occupying space), mithl (similar), lawāzim (concomitants), māhiyya (quiddity). These are foundational for kalam discussions on divine transcendence.
Similarity here is not physical resemblance but shared essential nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان السادس : لو كان تعالى مختصا بشيء من الأحياز والجهات لمكان مساويا للمتحيزات .. وهذا محال فذلك محال. بيان الملازمة : أنه تعالى لو كان مختصا بحيز، لكان معنى كونه شاغلا لذلك الحيز : كونه بحيث يمنع غيره عن أن يكون بحيث هو . ولو كان كذلك لكان متحيزا ، وقد بينا في الفصل المتقدم : أن المتحيزات بأسرها متماثلة في تمام الملاهية . فثبت : أنه تعالى لو كان متحيزا ، لكان مثلا لسائر المتحيزات . وإنما قلنا: إن ذلك محال . الأن المثلين يجب تساويهما في جميع اللوازم ، فيلزم إما قدم الكل ، وإما حدوث الكل ، وذلك محال
The sixth proof: If the Exalted were specified with any of the places and directions, He would be equal to the things occupying place.. And this is impossible, so that is impossible. Explanation of the connection: That if the Exalted were specified with a place, the meaning of His occupying that place would be that He is such that He prevents another from being where He is. And if that were the case, He would be a thing occupying place (mutahayyiz). And we have explained in the preceding chapter that things occupying place (mutahayyizāt) are all similar in complete quiddity. So it is established that if the Exalted were a thing occupying place, He would be similar to the rest of the things occupying place. And we say: That is impossible because similar things must be equal in all concomitants, so it would require either the eternity of all or the temporality of all, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is the sixth proof (al-burhān al-sādis) that Allah cannot be in a place. The argument proceeds in steps: 1) If Allah were in a place, He would occupy that space and prevent others from being there, meaning He is a 'thing occupying place' (mutahayyiz). 2) In a previous chapter, it was established that all things occupying place (bodies) are similar in their complete quiddity (māhiyya). 3) Therefore, if Allah were a body, He would be similar (mithl) to all other bodies. 4) Similar things must share all their concomitants (lawāzim). This would imply that either all (including Allah) are eternal or all are temporal—both absurd, given that Allah is eternal and creation is temporal. Hence, the initial assumption (that Allah is in a place) is impossible.

Key Terms
المتحيز
المثلان
اللوازم
الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'similar' here means physical resemblance in shape or size.
Correction: In kalam, similarity (mithliyya) means sharing the same essential quiddity (māhiyya). All bodies share the quiddity of being extended and occupying space, not necessarily specific physical features.

Checkpoint
What does Razi conclude would happen if Allah were similar to all bodies?
A) Allah would be limited in knowledge.
B) Allah would be composed of parts.
C) Either everything would be eternal or everything temporal.
D) Allah would be less powerful.

Key Takeaway
Razi's proof shows that placing Allah in space reduces Him to a body, which would erase His unique eternity and make creation co-eternal or temporal—both impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you ever unconsciously picture Him as being 'up there' in a specific direction? This proof shows that any spatial concept reduces Him to a body. What image of Allah have you been carrying that needs to be purified?
?
If you believe Allah is everywhere, have you considered that this might imply He occupies all space? How does this proof challenge that notion and push you to affirm His transcendence without spatial limitations?
?
The proof uses logical steps to guard Allah's unique eternity. Are there any areas in your belief where you have allowed a 'location' for Allah in your heart—perhaps thinking He is only present in a mosque or during a specific time? How can you cultivate a constant awareness of His transcendence without confining Him?

Objection and First Answer: Occupying Space Necessitates Bodily Essence
Razi counters the objection that spatial occupancy is accidental by analyzing its necessary implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's response to the objection that spatial occupancy is a mere attribute, and how he argues that it necessarily implies an essence with inherent extension (body).

Core Idea
Spatial occupancy is not a mere accident; it proves the essence is a body.

This passage presents a key objection to arguments for divine transcendence: perhaps being in a place is just a property, not part of the essence. Razi counters by analyzing what 'occupying space' truly entails. By identifying three inseparable rulings of a thing that occupies space, he shows that such a thing must be a body by essence. This lesson walks through that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the objector's claim: spatial occupancy is a ruling of the essence, not the essence itself, so equality in rulings doesn't mean equality in quiddity.
The objector tries to separate essence from its accidental properties.
2
Identify the three rulings of a thing occupying space
Razi lists three necessary properties of any mutahayyiz: occupying space, preventing others, and aggregability. Notice how each is described.
These three are presented as inseparable.
3
Understand Razi's conclusion
Razi argues that any essence described by these three rulings must have volume and magnitude inherently. This common concept of extension cannot be an attribute; it must be the essence itself.
This proves that such an essence is a body.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask: If being a body is essential for anything with these rulings, then how can one claim that spatial occupancy is merely accidental? This shows the objector's distinction collapses.
This is the first part of Razi's answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : حصول الشيء في الحيز ، وكونه مانعا لغيره من أن يحصل بحيث هو : حكم من أحكام الذات . ولا يلزم من الاستواء في الأحكام واللوازم : الاستواء فى الماهية . والجواب عنه من وجهين : الأول : إن المتحيز له أحكام ثلاثة : أحدها: أنه حاصل فى الحيز ، شاغل له و الثاني : كونه مانعا لغيره من أن يحصل بحيث هو : والثالث : كونه بحال لو ضم إليه أمثاله ، حصل له حجم كبير و مقدار عظيم . ولا شك أن كل ما يحصل في حيز . فقد حصل له هذه الأمور الثلاثة ، إلا أن الذات الموصوفة بهذه الأحكام الثلاثة ، لا بد وأن يكون له في نفسه الحجمية ويكون له فى نفسه المقدار . وهذا المعنى معقول مشترك بين كل الأحجام. ثم إنا دللنا على أن هذا المفهوم المشترك يمتنع أن يكون صفة لشيء آخر ، بل لابد وأن يكون ذاتا . وإذا كان كذلك.
If it is said: The obtaining of a thing in a place, and its preventing another from being where it is, are rulings of the essence. And equality in rulings and concomitants does not necessitate equality in quiddity. The answer is from two aspects: The first: That the thing occupying place (al-mutahayyiz) has three rulings: One: that it is obtained in the place, occupying it. Second: its preventing another from being where it is. Third: its being in a state such that if similars were added to it, it would have a large volume and great magnitude. And there is no doubt that everything that obtains in a place has obtained these three things. However, the essence described by these three rulings must necessarily have in itself volume and magnitude. And this meaning is intelligible and common among all volumes. Then we have proven that this common concept is impossible to be an attribute of something else, but must be an essence. And if that is so.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage contains an objection (فإن قيل) and the first part of the answer (الجواب). The objector argues that being in a place and preventing others from being there are merely rulings (ahkām) or accidents of the essence, not part of the essence itself. Therefore, equality in such rulings does not imply equality in quiddity. Razi answers by identifying what a thing occupying place (mutahayyiz) necessarily entails: it has three inseparable properties – occupying space, preventing others, and being capable of aggregation to form larger volumes. Any essence that has these properties must itself be inherently extended and possess magnitude (hajmiyya and miqdār). This common concept of extension cannot be an accidental attribute; it must be the essence itself. In other words, if something has these spatial properties, it is necessarily a body. The answer is cut off, but it continues the argument that such an essence cannot be attributed to Allah.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm)
الذات (al-dhāt)
الحجمية (al-hajmiyya)
المتحيز (al-mutahayyiz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spatial occupancy is a mere accidental attribute that does not affect the essence of a thing.
Correction: Razi demonstrates that being in a space necessarily entails inherent extension (volume and magnitude), which cannot be an accidental attribute but must be part of the essence itself. Hence, a thing with spatial properties is essentially a body.

Checkpoint
According to Razi’s answer, what is the significance of the three rulings of a thing occupying place?
A) They show that the thing is similar to others in quiddity.
B) They prove that the thing is a body with inherent extension.
C) They demonstrate that the thing is eternal.
D) They indicate that the thing is an attribute of Allah.

Key Takeaway
Spatial occupancy is not an accidental attribute; it necessitates that the essence itself is extended and thus a body, which cannot apply to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you ever unconsciously imagine Allah as being 'somewhere' above or in a direction? After learning that spatial occupancy necessarily implies being a body, how will you actively train your heart to think of Allah without spatial limitations starting with your next prayer?
?
Razi argues that volume (hajmiyya) cannot be an accident added to an essence but must be the essence itself. In your understanding of Allah's attributes (like power or mercy), do you ever treat them as accidental properties that could be added or removed? How can this lesson help you affirm that Allah's attributes are not separate from His essence?
?
The objector treated spatial occupancy as a mere 'ruling' that doesn't affect the core quiddity. Where in your own life do you keep matters of 'aqeedah at the level of intellectual accident—facts you assent to but that do not transform your heart? Name one specific theological truth from this lesson that you will carry from your mind to your soul this week, and how you will do it.

Objection and First Answer: Three Properties of a Body
Imam Razi presents an objection and the first of two answers, listing three properties of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's first answer to the objection that equality in judgments does not necessitate equality in essence, and how the three inseparable properties of spatial occupants lead to homogeneity of essences.

Core Idea
Three inseparable properties prove that all spatial occupants share the same essence.

In this passage, Imam Razi addresses a critical objection to the argument for divine transcendence. The objector claims that shared judgments do not imply shared essence. Razi's first answer reveals that for spatial occupants, three judgments are so fundamental that they define the essence itself, establishing homogeneity among all things that occupy space. This analysis sets the stage for the argument that God cannot be a spatial being.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the claim that equality in judgments does not necessitate equality in essence.
This is a common logical principle used by opponents.
2
Identify the three properties
Notice that these three properties are inseparable from any spatial occupant.
The text says 'the occupant of space has three judgments.'
3
Follow the reasoning to homogeneity
Razi argues that these properties define the essence of spatial occupants, making them all homogeneous in essence.
This strengthens the original argument against God being in space.
4
Reflect on implications for divine transcendence
If all spatial beings are homogeneous in essence, then God cannot be a spatial being because that would imply similarity to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : حصول الشيء في الحيز ، وكونه مانعا لغيره من أن يحصل بحيث هو : حكم من أحكام الذات . ولا يلزم من الاستواء في الأحكام واللوازم : الاستواء فى الماهية . والجواب عنه من وجهين : الأول : إن المتحيز له أحكام ثلاثة : أحدها: أنه حاصل فى الحيز ، شاغل له . و الثاني : كونه مانعا لغيره من أن يحصل بحيث هو . والثالث : كونه بحال لو ضم إليه أمثاله ، حصل له حجم كبير و مقدار عظيم . ولا شك أن كل ما يحصل في حيز . فقد حصل له هذه الأمور الثلاثة ، إلا أن الذات الموصوفة بهذه الأحكام الثلاثة ، لا بد وأن يكون له في نفسه الحجمية ويكون له في نفسه المقدار . وهذا المعنى معقول مشترك بين كل الأحجام. ثم إنا دللنا على أن هذا المفهوم المشترك يمتنع أن يكون صفة لشيء آخر ، بل لابد وأن يكون ذاتا . وإذا كان كذلك. فالمتحيزات فى ذواتها متماثلة ، والاختلاف إنما وقع في الصفات ، وحينئذ يحصل التقريب المذكور
If it is said: The occurrence of a thing in a space, and its being a preventer for others from occurring where it is, is a judgment among the judgments of the essence. And equality in judgments and concomitants does not necessitate equality in essence. The answer to it is from two aspects: The first: The occupant of space (al-mutahayyiz) has three judgments: one of them: that it occurs in space, occupying it; the second: its being a preventer for others from occurring where it is; the third: its being in a state such that if its likes were joined to it, it would acquire a large volume and great magnitude. There is no doubt that everything that occurs in space has these three matters, except that the essence described by these three judgments must have in itself volume (al-hajmiyya) and in itself magnitude (al-miqtar). And this meaning is intelligible and shared among all volumes. Then we demonstrated that this shared concept cannot be an attribute of something else, but must be an essence. And if that is so, then the occupants of space are homogeneous in their essences, and difference only occurs in attributes, and thus the aforementioned approximation occurs.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and the first of two answers. The objector argues that being in a space and preventing others from occupying that space are merely judgments (aḥkām) of the essence, and equality in such judgments does not necessitate equality in essence. Imam Razi responds with two answers. The first answer states that any occupant of space (al-mutahayyiz) necessarily has three inseparable properties: (1) it occupies space, (2) it prevents others from being where it is, and (3) if combined with its likes, it would produce a larger volume and magnitude. Every spatial occupant necessarily possesses these three, and the essence thus described must have in itself the concepts of volume and magnitude. This shared concept is intelligible and common to all volumes. Razi then argues that this common concept cannot be an accident (ṣifa) of something else; it must be the essence itself. Therefore, all spatial occupants are homogeneous (mutamāthila) in their essences, differing only in accidental attributes. This supports the earlier claim that if God were in a space, He would be like other spatial beings, which is impossible.

Key Terms
حيز
متحيز
أحكام
ماهية
تماثل
حجمية
مقدار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Equality in judgments never implies equality in essence.
Correction: When the judgments are inseparable and define the essence, as with the three properties of spatial occupants, equality in those judgments does imply equality in essence.

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, how many judgments are inseparably attached to every spatial occupant?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's first answer shows that the three inseparable properties of spatial occupants prove their essences are homogeneous, thereby refuting the objection and reinforcing that God cannot be in space.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The objector thought equality in some properties doesn’t imply equality in essence. Are there ways you treat God as if He shares properties with creation—like being limited by time or place—without realizing it? Examine your thoughts: do you ever subconsciously confine God to a mosque, a direction, or a moment? What will you do to actively combat that assumption?
?
Razi proves that all bodies are homogeneous in essence, so if God were a body, He would be just like other bodies. Does your belief in God's uniqueness truly rule out any likeness to creation, or do you hold onto comfortable anthropomorphic ideas? Identify one mental image or statement about God that you need to correct based on this lesson, and resolve to replace it with the proper understanding of His transcendence.

Second Answer: Shared Accidents Do Not Entail Shared Essence
Imam Razi's second answer showing the objection's self-defeating nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi argues that accepting the opponent's objection would actually undermine the proof of the temporality of bodies, because shared judgments do not imply shared essences.

Core Idea
Shared judgments do not prove shared essences, so the objection backfires.

Imam Razi now offers the second answer to the objection that all spatial things must be homogeneous. He points out a fatal flaw: even if the objection were valid, it would destroy the opponent's own position. By showing that shared accidents do not entail shared essence, Razi turns the tables. Let's see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if valid... then you cannot...'
2
Identify the logical chain
Trace the steps: (1) if objection valid, (2) then cannot affirm homogeneity, (3) because shared judgment ≠ shared essence, (4) then possible necessary atoms, (5) proof of temporality fails.
This chain is the core of the argument.
3
Understand the consequence
Why does this undermine the opponent? The opponent relies on the proof of temporality for all bodies; if some atoms can be necessary, the proof does not apply to them.
Razi shows the objection is self-defeating.
4
Reflect on the key terms
Consider the terms تماثل الجواهر (homogeneity of atoms), حكم (judgment), ماهية (essence), and how they relate to the argument.
These terms are central to kalam discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني : إن السؤال الذي ذكر تم - إن صح - فحينئذ لا يمكنكم القطع بتماثل الجواهر ، لاحتمال أن يقال : الجواهر ، وإن اشتركت في الحصول في الحيز ، إلا أن هذا الاشتراك في حكم من الأحكام والاشتراك في الحكم لا يقتضي الاشتراك في الماهية ، وإذا لم يثبت كون الجواهر متماثلة ، فحينئذ لا يبعد في العقل وجود جواهر مختصة بأحيازها على سبيل الوجوب ، بحيث يمتنع خروجها عن تلك الأحياز ، وحينئذ لا يطرد دليل حدوث الأجسام في تلك الأشياء . وعلى هذا التقدير لا يمكنكم القطع بحدوث كل الأجسام والله أعلم
And the second aspect: Indeed the question that was mentioned is complete — if it is valid — then you cannot decisively affirm the homogeneity of atoms (jawāhir), because it is possible to say: Atoms, even if they share in occurring in space, this sharing is in a judgment among judgments, and sharing in judgment does not necessitate sharing in essence. And if the homogeneity of atoms is not established, then it is not improbable in reason that there exist atoms specifically attached to their spaces necessarily, such that their departure from those spaces is impossible, and then the proof of the temporality of bodies does not apply to those things. And on this estimation you cannot decisively affirm the temporality of all bodies. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage contains the second answer to the objection. Imam Razi argues that even if the objection were sound, it would undermine the opponent's own position. If the objector claims that sharing a judgment (like occupying space) does not entail sharing in essence (māhiyya), then the opponent cannot be certain that all atoms are homogeneous. If atoms are not proven homogeneous, then it is rationally possible that some atoms necessarily occupy their spaces and cannot leave them. This would break the standard proof for the temporality of bodies (ḥudūth al-ajsām), which relies on the premise that all spatial things are contingent and temporally originated. Thus, the objection backfires: accepting it would prevent certainty about the temporality of all bodies, which is a core doctrine. Razi ends with 'and God knows best' (wa-llāhu aʿlam).

Key Terms
تماثل الجواهر
حكم
ماهية
حدوث الأجسام
اشتراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Admitting that atoms might not be homogeneous only helps safeguard divine transcendence without any negative consequences.
Correction: Razi shows that accepting this possibility actually undermines the proof of the temporality of all bodies, which is a core kalam doctrine. The objection backfires.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The second answer reveals that the objection, if accepted, demolishes the proof of the temporality of bodies, thereby protecting divine transcendence at the cost of a core kalam doctrine.

Seventh Proof: Direction Implies Composition
Imam Razi presents the seventh proof: being in a direction entails composition, an infinite regress, or absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's seventh proof that Allah cannot be in a direction because it leads to absurd consequences such as composition or identity of opposites.

Core Idea
Direction implies composition; composition is impossible for God.

Imam Razi presents a clever reductio ad absurdum. The argument assumes that if Allah were in a direction, He would be 'great' (not a point). Then it examines the implications of His facing the Throne, showing that both possible scenarios lead to impossibility. Let's trace the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the assumption
Recognize that the proof begins by noting that anyone who says Allah is in a direction necessarily says He is great—no one says He is like a tiny point.
This sets up the premise that direction implies greatness, not smallness.
2
Examine the first alternative
Consider the side facing the right of the Throne. If it is the same side as the one facing the left, then right and left are identical, which is absurd.
That would reduce the Throne to an indivisible atom.
3
Examine the second alternative
If the side facing the right is different from the side facing the left, then Allah has multiple sides, implying composition—impossible for God.
Thus both alternatives are false.
4
Conclude the proof
Since both options lead to absurdity, the original assumption that Allah is in a direction must be false.
This refutes those who claim Allah occupies space.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان السابع : إنه لو كان تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز ، المكان عظما . لأنه ليس في العقلاء من يقول : إنه مختص بجهة ، ومع ذلك فإنه في الحقارة مثل النقطة التي لا تنقسم ، ومثل الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ . بل كل من قال : إنه مختص بالجهة والحيز ، قال : إنه عظيم في الذات . وإذا كان كذلك ، فنقول : الجانب الذي منه يحاذى يمين العرش . إما أن يكون هو الجانب الذي منه يحاذى يسار العرش ، أو غيره . والأول باطل ، لأنه إن عقل ذلك ، فلم لا يعقل أن يقال : إن يمين العرش عين يسار العرش حتى يقال : العرش على عظمته ، مثل الجوهر الفرد ، والجزء الذي لا يتجزأ ؟ وذلك لا يقوله عاقل . والثاني أيضا باطل ، لأن على هذا التقدير تكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء
The seventh proof: If He, exalted, were specific to direction and space, He would necessarily be great. Because there is none among rational people who says that He is specific to a direction and yet He is in lowliness like the indivisible point and like the part that is not divided. Rather, everyone who says He is specific to direction and space says He is great in essence. And if that is so, we say: The side from which He faces the right of the Throne — either it is the side from which He faces the left of the Throne, or something else. The first is false, because if that is intelligible, why is it not intelligible to say that the right of the Throne is identical to its left, such that it would be said that the Throne, despite its greatness, is like the indivisible atom and the part that is not divided? And no rational person says that. The second is also false, because on this estimation the essence of God, exalted, would be composed of parts.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof against the claim that God is in a direction or space. The proof begins by noting that anyone who asserts that God occupies a direction also asserts that God is great (ʿaẓīm) in essence — no one says He is like a point or indivisible part. Given that, if God faces the right side of the Throne, then either that same side is also facing the left side of the Throne, or it is a different side. The first option is impossible because it would mean the right and left of the Throne are identical, reducing the Throne to an indivisible atom, which is absurd. The second option implies that God has distinct sides, meaning He is composed of parts (ajzāʾ), which is impossible for God. Thus, both alternatives are false, so the initial assumption that God is in a direction is false.

Key Terms
جهة
حيز
عظيم
نقطة لا تنقسم
جزء لا يتجزأ
مركبة من الأجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some imagine that directionalism implies God is like a tiny point or indivisible atom.
Correction: Razi explicitly says that no rational person says God is lowly like a point; rather, directionalism implies greatness, which then leads to composition.

Checkpoint
What does the seventh proof conclude if God's side facing the right of the Throne is different from the side facing the left?
A) He is like the Throne
B) He is composed of parts
C) He is indivisible
D) He has no direction

Key Takeaway
Razi's seventh proof shows that God being in a direction leads to either absurd identity or composition, both impossible, so direction is negated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Razi argues that directionalism leads to absurdity. Is there any belief you hold about God that, if followed to its logical conclusion, would lead to an absurdity? Are you willing to let go of that belief?

The Seventh Proof: Spatial Location Implies Composition
Imam al-Razi presents the seventh proof against spatial location for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of Imam al-Razi's seventh proof, which refutes the attribution of spatial location to Allah by demonstrating that it necessarily leads to the absurdity of composition and change in the Divine Essence.

Core Idea
Spatial location for God implies composition, which is impossible for the Divine.

This lesson presents a dense reductio ad absurdum argument from Imam al-Razi. The proof systematically examines the logical consequences of claiming that Allah is confined to a direction. It shows that such a claim forces one to accept that Allah has parts, which then leads to further absurdities. Work through each step carefully to see how the argument eliminates every possible escape route.

Guided Path
1
Establish the premise
Understand that if Allah is in a direction, He must be a body. No one claims He is like an indivisible atom; rather, they say He is great.
This sets the stage for the argument.
2
The dilemma of God's relation to the Throne
Consider the side facing the right of the Throne: is it the same as or different from the side facing the left? Both options are examined.
This is a classic dichotomous argument.
3
First possibility: same side
If the sides are identical, then the right and left of the Throne would also be identical, reducing the Throne to an indivisible point—absurd.
Quickly dismissed.
4
Second possibility: different sides leads to composition
If the sides are different, then Allah's essence has distinct parts. These parts are either similar or different in essence. Each leads to impossibility.
This is the core of the proof.
5
Analyze similar parts
If parts are similar, they can be adjacent or separated. But similars share all possibilities, so adjacent parts could become separated and vice versa, implying change and composition—impossible for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان السابع : إنه لو كان تعالى مختصا بالجهة والحيز، لكان عظما. لأنه ليس في العقلاء من يقول: إنه مختص بجهة، ومع ذلك فإنه في الحقارة مثل النقطة التي لا تنقسم، ومثل الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ. بل كل من قال: إنه مختص بالجهة والحيز، قال: إنه عظيم في الذات. وإذا كان كذلك، فنقول: الجانب الذي منه يحاذي يمين العرش إما أن يكون هو الجانب الذي منه يحاذي يسار العرش، أو غيره. والأول باطل، لأنه إن عقل ذلك، فلم لا يعقل أن يقال: إن يمين العرش عين يسار العرش حتى يقال: العرش على عظمته، مثل الجوهر الفرد، والجزء الذي لا يتجزأ؟ وذلك لا يقوله عاقل. والثاني أيضا باطل، لأن على هذا التقدير تكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء. ثم تلك الأجزاء إما أن تكون متماثلة الماهية، أو مختلفة الماهية. والأول: محال. لأن على هذا التقدير يكون بعض تلك الأجزاء المتماثلة متباعدة، وبعضها متلاقية، والمثلان يصح على كل واحد منهما ما يصح على الآخر. فعلى هذا يلزم القطع بأنه يصح على المتلاقيين أن يصيرا متباعدين، وعلى المتباعدين أن يصيرا متلاقيين: وذلك يقتضي جواز الاجتماع والافتراق على ذات الله تعالى، وهو محال. وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: إن تلك الأجزاء مختلفة في الماهية. فلابد وأن ينتهي تحليل تركيبه إلى أجزاء، يكون كل واحد منها مبرأ عن التركيب، لأن التركيب عبارة عن اجتماع الوحدات. ولولا حصول الوحدات لما عقل اجتماعه ما. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول: إن كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء البسيطة، لا بد وأن يماس كل واحد منها بيمينه شيئا، وبيساره شيئا آخر. لكن يمينه مثل يساره. وإلا لكان في نفسه مركبا. وقد فرضناه غير مركب. هذا خلف. وإذا ثبت أن يمينه مثل يساره، وثبت أن المثلين لابد وأن يشتركا في جميع اللوازم لزم القطع بأن ممسوس يمينه، يصح أن يصير ممسوس يساره، وبالعكس. ومتى صح ذلك، فقد صح التفرق والانحلال على تلك الأجزاء. وحينئذ يعود الأمر إلى جواز الاجتماع والافتراق على ذات الله تعالى. وهو محال. فثبت: أن القول بكونه في جهة من الجهات يفضي إلى هذه المحالات، فيكون القول به محالا. وبالله التوفيق.
The seventh proof: If He, exalted, were confined to direction and location, He would be a body. For there is no rational person who says He is confined to a direction and yet He is in lowliness like an indivisible point and like an atom. Rather, everyone who says He is confined to direction and location says He is great in essence. And if that is so, we say: The side that faces the right of the Throne is either the side that faces the left of the Throne, or something else. The first is false, because if that is conceivable, then why is it not conceivable to say that the right of the Throne is the same as the left of the Throne, so that it would be said: The Throne, despite its greatness, is like the indivisible atom and the part that does not divide? No rational person would say that. The second is also false, because on this assumption the essence of God, exalted, would be composed of parts. Then those parts are either similar in essence or different in essence. The first is impossible, because on this assumption some of those similar parts would be separated and some adjacent, and for two similars whatever is possible for one is possible for the other. Thus it necessarily follows that it is possible for the adjacent ones to become separated and for the separated ones to become adjacent, and that entails the possibility of conjunction and separation for the essence of God, exalted, which is impossible. As for the second division—that those parts are different in essence—the analysis of His composition must terminate in parts each of which is free from composition, because composition is the joining of units. Without the existence of units, their joining would not be conceivable. If this is established, we say: Each one of those simple parts must touch something with its right and something else with its left. But its right is like its left; otherwise it would itself be composite, but we have assumed it non-composite—a contradiction. And if it is established that its right is like its left, and it is established that two similars must share all concomitants, then it necessarily follows that what is touched by its right can become touched by its left, and vice versa. And if that is possible, then separation and dissolution of those parts is possible. Then the matter reverts to the possibility of conjunction and separation for the essence of God, exalted, which is impossible. Thus it is established that the statement that He is in a direction leads to these impossibilities, so the statement is impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof against the attribution of spatial location (jiha or hayyiz) to God. It is a reductio ad absurdum argument. The author first establishes a premise: anyone who claims God is in a direction also necessarily claims He is great in essence (not small like a point). Then he examines the relation of God to the Throne. If God faces the Throne, then the side of God that faces the right of the Throne is either the same as the side that faces the left or different. If it were the same, that would imply the Throne's right and left are identical, reducing the Throne to an indivisible atom—absurd. If they are different, then God's essence would have distinct sides, implying composition (tarkib). The argument then analyzes composition: if composed of similar parts, those parts would be either adjacent or separated; but since similars share all possibilities, they could become separated or adjacent, implying change and composition for God, which is impossible. If composed of different parts, the analysis must break down to simple, non-composite parts. Each simple part has a right and left, which are similar; otherwise the part would itself be composite. Since the right and left are similar, what touches the right can touch the left, allowing separation and dissolution of the parts—again impossible for God. The conclusion is that the attribution of direction leads to absurdities, so it is false.

Key Terms
جهة
حيز
تركيب
تماثل
جوهر فرد
جزء لا يتجزأ
اجتماع
افتراق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah is spatially located, He must be small like an atom.
Correction: The proof shows that even if He is considered great, spatial location leads to composition, which is impossible for the Divine.

Checkpoint
In the seventh proof, what is the first possibility considered regarding the side of Allah facing the right of the Throne?
A) It is the same as the side facing the left of the Throne.
B) It is different from the side facing the left of the Throne.
C) It is neither same nor different.
D) It is unknown.

Key Takeaway
Attributing spatial location to Allah leads to composition and change, which is impossible for the Necessary Being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Does your mental image of Allah ever include a sense of direction—like up, above the sky, or in a specific place? This proof shows that such thinking leads to absurdities. What habit can you adopt to constantly remind yourself that Allah is beyond all spatial limitations, especially during worship?
?
The argument relies on logical necessity. If someone asked you tomorrow why you believe Allah is not in a place, could you give a rational answer grounded in this proof? What step will you take to make this understanding deeply rooted in your heart, not just your mind?
?
If you truly internalize that Allah is free from location, then your awareness of His presence cannot depend on being in a mosque or a quiet room. In what situation do you most struggle to feel His closeness? What concrete change can you make today to live with the reality that He is always near, without being confined anywhere?
